Qingdao: Japanese Troops Still Not Withdrawing; Oikawa Holds Important Meeting After Arriving in Qingdao; Japanese Troops Present Unreasonable Demands to Municipal Government; Our Authorities Promulgate Measures to Maintain Public Order 67

Qingdao Correspondence: The illegal landing of Japanese naval infantry in Qingdao has been under negotiation by the Municipal Government with the Japanese Consulate and the Japanese military authorities for days, but they have not yet withdrawn. Oikawa, the commander of the Japanese Third Fleet, arrived in Qingdao aboard his flagship Izumo on the morning of the 5th. He held an important meeting on the Izumo in the morning, and then continued the meeting at 3 PM at the residence of the Japanese naval attaché. Attendees included Watajiri, staff officer of the North China Garrison Army, Haga, head of the special service agency, Consul General Nishiharu Hiko, Consul Tawaki, staff officers of the Third Fleet, and the captains of various ships. The meeting lasted for four hours, during which they finalized the demands to be made to the municipal government. Consul General Nishiharu Hiko visited Mayor Shen Honglie at 5 PM on the evening of the 5th to begin negotiations. According to sources from the Japanese side, the Japanese military is demanding a great number of conditions from the municipal government. It is said that Mayor Shen is determined not to accept Japan's unreasonable demands and will not resume negotiations until the Japanese navy has completely withdrawn. It is also reported that the municipal government has strengthened security in the city and is prepared to ensure safety. Furthermore, after Oikawa's arrival in Qingdao, he originally planned to meet with Mayor Shen on the morning of the 6th, but his fleet adjutant, Yasuda, informed Zhou Jiayan, an advisor to the Municipal Government, that Oikawa's visit to Qingdao was initially intended to meet with Mayor Shen and reminisce, but unfortunately, a local incident occurred. He stated that they would schedule a meeting after a complete and peaceful resolution.

Emergency Measures to Maintain Public Order

The Municipal Government, considering the labor unrest occurring at Japanese-owned cotton mills in the city and Japan's dispatch of over ten warships under the pretext of protecting its nationals, has noted the increasingly tense situation and fears that criminals may take the opportunity to cause disturbances and disrupt public order. Therefore, it has jointly issued emergency measures to maintain public order with the headquarters of our Third Naval Fleet. The proclamation and measures are recorded below: A. Proclamation: "Considering that the city is currently facing a tight winter defense and that labor unrest has occurred, the importance of local public order cannot be overstated. Fearing that criminals may take the opportunity to cause disturbances or deliberately spread rumors and confuse the public, the emergency measures to maintain public order promulgated by the National Government on February 20 of this year should be strictly implemented. This proclamation is hereby issued to all sectors of the public for their information and strict compliance." B. Measures: (1) In the event of disturbances of order, instigation of riots, disruption of traffic, or other incidents endangering the nation, military and police responsible for public order may use force or other effective means to stop them. (2) In the event that someone uses writing, drawings, speeches, or other methods to promote the aforementioned crimes, they may be arrested on the spot, and resistance may be suppressed with force or other effective means if necessary. (3) Military and police encountering assemblies or parades that disturb order or incite the public shall immediately disperse them and may arrest the ringleaders and those who resist dispersal. (4) Military and police encountering the aforementioned incidents shall immediately disarm and arrest those carrying weapons on the spot, and may search for and arrest suspects. (5) Those who knowingly harbor, shelter, or conceal individuals who violate these measures may be arrested. (6) Military and police handling incidents shall immediately report to their superior officers, and those arrested shall be immediately sent to the nearest military police commander, public security bureau chief, squadron leader, or inspector for questioning and dealt with according to the circumstances, in accordance with the Emergency Punishment Law for Endangering the Republic of China or other criminal laws. (7) Military and police handling incidents in accordance with these measures shall protect the people who strictly observe discipline and shall pay attention to maintaining public order and restoring normalcy. Mayor Shen Honglie, Commander Xie Gangzhe.

After Several Counterattacks, the Bandits and Puppets Were Defeated; A Certain Army Assembles to Participate in the Battle; Bandit Troops Now Gathered at Damiaozi and Shangdu; A Certain Army Draws 3,000 Men from Various Units; Ulanqab League’s Prince Pan Wang Also Leads Troops to Attack Bandit Troops 68

Special Dispatch from Suiyuan: After being defeated by our army on the morning of the 3rd, the puppet bandits who counterattacked Bailingmiao, with four to five thousand bandits, launched another counterattack on our army's front lines at around 2 PM that afternoon, under the cover of aircraft from a certain country. Until after dusk, they launched five or six continuous attacks. Under the intense artillery fire, our army calmly fought back and once again repelled the bandit army. The bandits suffered over 500 casualties. Our army captured a great number of spoils of war. In the vicinity of Bailingmiao after the battle, a large number of defeated and fleeing soldiers were found. Our army treated them kindly and provided relief. At dawn on the morning of the 4th, the bandits launched another full-scale attack on Bailingmiao. In addition to gathering forces from nearby mountains, a large number of bandit troops were also transferred from Damiaozi, the bandit headquarters in northern Suiyuan. Under the cover of artillery, aircraft, and armored vehicles from a certain country, they launched a fierce attack on our positions. At this time, the morale of our army was even higher, and they bravely fought back. After several hours of intense fighting, including hand-to-hand combat, our army launched a counterattack at noon, and the bandits were unable to withstand it. They scattered and fled in different directions. Some fled by vehicle under the cover of aircraft from a certain country, some fled in disarray, and some were dying from cold and hunger. The dead and wounded were piled up like pillows, a pitiful sight. One of the bandit army's captains led over 300 men and surrendered to our side. Our side has always been lenient to those who surrender and treated them favorably. The remaining defeated soldiers are also being taken in and relieved. The bandit army suffered heavy losses in this battle and scattered in disarray. Currently, there are no bandit traces within fifty to sixty li of Bailingmiao. Our army is actively setting up defensive works and is looking for opportunities to eliminate the remaining bandits.

According to the surrendering bandits, "The bandit troops have not eaten for two days and are suffering from hunger and cold. The morale of the troops is low, and the bandit troops were either coerced or deceived into coming. Since their arrival was not their wish, who would be willing to die for nothing? Therefore, everyone lacks the will to fight. Moreover, from afar, they heard that compatriots across the country were donating money to save the country. We are all Chinese, and who has no conscience? Therefore, they are determined to uphold the principle that Chinese should not fight Chinese. Therefore, when the national army arrives, they all wish to surrender." Currently, the gathering points of the bandit forces are Damiaozi in northern Suiyuan and Shangdu in northern Chahar. In Damiaozi, there are over 2,000 men from the Shi Ying bandit unit, over 1,000 men from the Prince De bandit unit, and smaller units from Jin Jia, Li Shouxin, and other bandit units, totaling no more than 5,000 men. In Shangdu, there are five to six thousand men from Li Shouxin's bandit army, over 1,000 men from Prince De's bandit army, and a puppet army unit. In addition, the puppet regime has transferred a unit of puppet troops from each military district in Rehe, which has now arrived in Guyuan. It is reported that a certain side has transferred a small portion of men from various units of a certain army, totaling 3,000 men, who will also go to the front lines to participate in the war. However, our army's defenses in both eastern and northern Suiyuan are extremely solid, and the bandit forces will hardly succeed.

The Ulanqab League's Sizi Wang Banner is located in a strategic area. Since the situation in northern Suiyuan became tense, the banner's environment has also become tense. Later, after Bailingmiao was captured by the national army, the fleeing bandit troops were attacked by the banner's security team, and the bandit troops suffered significant losses. Recently, the bandit side prepared to counterattack and infiltrated the banner's border from the Taolin grassland. On the 1st of this month, they engaged in a fierce battle with the security team led by Jasaq Pandegong Chabu of the banner. The fighting continued on the 2nd and 3rd. It is reported that nearby stationed troops have been ordered to go there, hoping to join forces with Prince Pan's cavalry to eliminate the bandit puppets.

Wounded Soldiers' Enthusiasm

This reporter visited the Fourth Elementary School Wounded Soldiers Hospital on the afternoon of the 5th to comfort the wounded soldiers. Mr. Yun Hanzhang, a military medical officer at the hospital, guided the tour. The hospital is using the facilities of the Fourth Elementary School. The buildings are spacious, well-lit, and the interior is clean. The food and all equipment meet hygiene standards. Mr. Yun also gives regular talks to lightly wounded soldiers, imparting various knowledge. After offering my condolences, I was able to briefly talk with Mr. Wang, who was less severely wounded, about the situation at the front lines. According to Mr. Wang, "We soldiers are indebted to the nation for nurturing us. Our duty is to defend the country and protect the people. Now that the bandits and puppets are invading, it is our duty to eliminate the bandits. The national army soldiers and brothers who participated in this battle all understand this principle. As soon as they hear of the bandit army, they bravely rush forward, with a spirit of advancing without retreating and having me without an enemy, hoping to wipe them out in one fell swoop. Therefore, wherever the national army goes, the bandit army is like withered leaves and rotten branches, collapsing and fleeing. All the soldiers and brothers are honored to be able to go to the front lines and kill the enemy, and they are ashamed of not being sent to the front lines. Even the wounded brothers do not want to retreat. Except for those who are discovered by the medical team and carried to the rear for treatment, many wounded brothers endure the pain and continue to kill the enemy without being willing to go to the rear for recuperation. Once our injuries are slightly better, we are determined to go to the front lines again to kill the bandits and protect the national territory," and so on.

People's Militia's Indignation

After leaving the Wounded Soldiers Hospital, this reporter went to the small school ground to visit the Suiyuan Anti-Communist Self-Defense Corps' Regular Detachment Training Department. The Regular Detachment is composed of people's militia recruited from various counties, with each term lasting four months and consisting of 3,000 people. Upon arriving at the department, the entire Regular Detachment was gathered on the parade ground, listening to a speech by a certain committee member. The training director of the detachment is Mr. Li Dachao. The soldiers stood straight in the cold wind for over an hour, without showing any signs of shivering. It is said that the soldiers in this term have only been training for two months, but their order and spirit are quite good. After the certain committee member's speech ended, this reporter gathered several team members in a corner of the parade ground and spoke for a short while, learning that they all possess patriotic fervor. According to them, after this training, they will use the military knowledge and skills they have learned to teach other villagers upon returning to their hometowns, in order to organize the villagers in each village, so that each village becomes an organized and united unit, to bear the responsibility of defending the local area and eliminating traitorous bandits. In the future, they can also serve as the rear guard for the regular army and perform various necessary tasks in the rear. The current situation in Suiyuan is critical. If the villagers do not unite to defend themselves and the country, they will not even be able to become slaves like the people of Korea and Taiwan. Who does not have parents, wives, and children? Who does not have ancestors' graves? Rather than seeking to be slaves in the future and not being able to obtain it, why not sacrifice everything now to protect the national territory? Therefore, they are now preparing to sacrifice everything to serve as the rear guard for the army, and so on. From this, one can glimpse the flourishing of Suiyuan's public spirit.

Patriotism of Prostitutes

While the Suiyuan soldiers are valiantly and relentlessly suppressing the bandit puppets, the prostitutes in the rear are also filled with patriotic thoughts. Therefore, they have elected representatives to comfort the wounded soldiers and donate money to comfort the soldiers. The prostitutes have declared to the outside world, "We are all Chinese, and each of us has a share in loving the country. If the Suiyuan region is invaded by bandits and puppets, our relatives will be slaughtered by the traitorous bandits and will not be able to survive. Therefore, although the occupation of prostitutes is pitiful and our strength is meager, our hearts for loving the country are the same," and so on.

Soldiers Volunteering

After the outbreak of the Suiyuan war, the national army soldiers were deeply indignant and all wished to go to the battlefield to kill the bandits as soon as possible. Soldiers who had not been transferred to the front lines mostly volunteered to their superiors. The following is the original text of the request from the Provisional Cavalry Company to Commander-in-Chief Fu Zuoyi, which shows a glimpse of the morale: "To Commander-in-Chief: This is a report from all the soldiers of the Cavalry Company of the Fourth Regiment. Now that the national crisis is at hand, it is extremely urgent. Only because our regiment has already gone to the front lines to resist the enemy, we are determined to pursue and eliminate the puppet bandits. Our company has not gone to the front lines to participate in the battle. We ask the Commander-in-Chief, all the soldiers of our company are willing to go to the front lines to resist the enemy. We are determined that there must be a reason why our company has not departed, but we do not know what kind of responsibility we bear that we have not gone. We soldiers are very ashamed because we eat from the country and wear from the country, but when the time comes, we are not needed. Our public raises us in vain. If there is another opportunity, we hope that the Commander-in-Chief will let our company participate no matter what. It is the wish of all the soldiers in our company to sacrifice for the country without hesitation. Since the mobilization order was issued, we have been preparing day and night, and our hearts are very happy and our spirits are greatly increased. Until now, we have not gone to the front lines to pursue and eliminate the puppet bandits. The soldiers feel unhappy in their hearts. It is not that we are afraid of death, it is just that all the soldiers in our company are also very willing to sacrifice. Even if we sacrifice, it is the duty of a soldier to die on the front lines rather than be a slave to a conquered nation. This is the goal of all the soldiers in our company. Asking the Commander-in-Chief is safe. Written and stamped by Sergeant Tian Puzhen, Liu Baolan, Yang Hanwu, Li Ziwen, and six other people from the Provisional Cavalry Company." (6th)

Changshu 70

Promoting the Comfort Bag Movement

The Women's Association here has recently decided to promote the "Women's Comfort Bag Movement," advocating the use of items needed on the front lines to comfort the Jin-Sui soldiers, and thereby inspire the patriotic enthusiasm of the Changshu women's community. These comfort bags are made of domestic green cloth, the size of a Boy Scout's dry food bag, containing medicines, first aid supplies, food, and a thermos, etc. The mouth of the bag is sealed by the women themselves, and the bag also contains a letter written by the women to encourage the soldiers, so that the soldiers will be even more courageous in their loyalty upon receiving it. Now, once a sufficient number has been collected, they will be handed over to the county authorities for delivery to the front lines.

Wuxi 71

Cold Weather, First Snowfall

Since the beginning of winter, the weather has been dry with no rain, and the cold has been extreme. On the morning of the 7th, thick clouds covered the sky, as if it would rain, and the weather felt even colder. The Fahrenheit thermometer dropped to 43.7 degrees. At 3:40 PM, snowflakes suddenly fell, dancing in the wind, melting as soon as they hit the ground, and did not stop until evening. This is the first auspicious snowfall seen this winter.

Fire Destroys Entire Village

In the Dongwang Village Qianxiang area of Liu'an Town, the fifth district of the county, there are more than ten families of villagers, mostly surnamed Mao, who are engaged in agriculture. At around 7 PM on the afternoon of the 6th, Mao Axing, Mao Ahong, Mao Jinbao, and other families were suddenly careless. At that time, the wind was strong and the fire was fierce. The villagers' houses were mostly made of wood and firewood, which easily caught fire, so it quickly became uncontrollable, spreading to Mao Tingzheng, Mao Sanmazi, Mao Genxing, Mao Er'an, Mao Ronglin, Mao Kun Gen, Mao Quan Gen, and more than twenty other families, with more than ninety houses destroyed, resulting in losses of tens of thousands. Now, the affected families are wailing and crying loudly. The town head, Mao Jinshan, is collecting donations on their behalf to provide relief.

Danyang 72

Robbery Occurs in Binjiang Township

Zhang Jinlian, a farmer in Buliangzhou, Binjiang Township, the eighth district of the county, had some wealth, which attracted the covetousness of bandits. On the night of the 5th, a number of bandits suddenly broke into the house with sharp weapons. At that time, Zhang and her sister were both in the room. The bandits tied them up with ropes and forced them to tell where the hidden silver was. After a slight hesitation, they were whipped. Then, Zhang's sister was burned with fire, causing her to be covered in burns. Zhang and others could not bear the pain and spat out the truth, resulting in more than fifty yuan in cash and various clothes and jewelry being stolen.

Nantong 73

In the counties under the jurisdiction of Jiangbei Tong, it was阴 cold on the 7th, and the temperature was even lower in the afternoon. Hail fell at 3 PM, and snowflakes fluttered at 6 PM. This is the first snow seen after the beginning of winter.

Yangzhou 74

No Wheat Sprouts in the Four Townships

In the western townships of Jiangdu, there has been a severe drought since autumn. Most of the wheat planting required waterwheel irrigation. The fields planted on high ground barely planted during the slight rain and muddy softness. Except for the fields near the river, none have sprouted to this day. Even in the Jiuzhong Bridge area around the North Lake, because the lake water has dried up in winter, although the wheat has sprouted, it has now withered. Since the beginning of winter, there has been no rain or snow. Due to the severe cold and drought, farmers have abandoned their homes and gone to Jiangnan to seek food. Farmers from Huaihai have also come to Yangzhou. Seeing that the situation is not good, they have also crossed the river. On the 4th and 5th, various counties in Jiangnan expelled those from Jiangbei returning to their hometowns in an endless stream, all passing through the Dongguan area of this county. They are gathering in groups of three to five, begging for food and heading north together.

Wanfu Bridge Project Completed

The Wanfu Bridge project in the eastern township of Yangzhou City is now nearing completion. Xu Zhongchang and Zhan Shouduan, teachers of the engineering department of the Provincial Yangzhou High School, went to visit on the 6th and plan to lead all the students of the D class to the site for surveying and practice within three days.

Zhen'an Ship Hits Embankment While Passing Through Lock

The Zhen'an ship of the New Transport Company was traveling south from upstream on the afternoon of the 6th. After passing through the Shaobo Ship Lock, it intended to dock on the east bank. However, because the ship was traveling too fast, it hit the old site of the west embankment, and the ship was stuck in the mud and could not turn sideways. It sounded its whistle for help. Just when it was critical, the Xinbaohe ship of the Fuyun Company's Zhenyou shuttle passed by and tried to pull it out. It took forty minutes to get out of danger.

The staff of various party and government agencies in this county have implemented saving one day's salary to comfort the soldiers on the Suiyuan front. On the 7th, the students of Sheyang Middle School also saved money from snacks and got 30 yuan in national currency, which was also donated to comfort the soldiers on the Suiyuan front.

Gaoyou 76

Severe Cold, Thin Ice on Water

Since the beginning of winter in this county, the weather has been mild. The weather suddenly became severely cold on the 5th, and it was even worse at night. Thin ice has formed on the water, and the thermometer suddenly dropped to 30 degrees. The poor are suffering greatly.

Haizhou 77

Criminals in Guanyun Arrested

Liu Xiaoliu, a habitual criminal in Shimenkou Village, the second district of Guanyun County, has been repeatedly pursued by local authorities but has not been captured. The day before yesterday, Xiaoliu returned home at night and was detected by Huang Shijie, the head of the township, who secretly led strong men to capture Xiaoliu and escort him to the Third Battalion of the Third Regiment of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Corps at Dayishan. After strict interrogation by the battalion headquarters, Xiaoliu confessed to being a bandit and confessed that he had recently robbed Xia Xishan's family in Chuanxing Village, Donghai District, and kidnapped Bian Xishan's son Bian Xiaokao, and Xia Xirong's son Xia Xiaoyin, all hiding in a certain family in Shimenkou. After hearing the confession, the battalion commander immediately sent a team led by Xiaoliu to the home of a certain family in Shimenkou and rescued the two hostages. The entire family of a certain surname all fled in fear of crime.

Huaiyin 78

The prisoners in prison and the people serving reform through labor in the seventh district of this county, sympathizing with the aid to Suiyuan, have successively saved food to raise money and handed it over to the One-Day Movement Promotion Committee for transfer to the front lines to comfort the soldiers. It is estimated that the male and female prisoners in the county prison saved one day's food, earning more than 19 yuan. The 831 male and female prisoners in the seventh district have saved food for three days since the 1st of this month, earning 93 yuan, five corners, and six cents.

Ningbo 79

Details of Liquor Shop Tax Evasion Case

Chen Sheng Liquor Shop in the western suburbs of this port was found to have evaded donations and taxes by Xiang Pi Zhen, a supervising committee member of the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance. He often took the account books of the shop to the Yin-Feng Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau for thorough investigation. It is now known that the owner of the shop, Lou Ruxin, is a local business leader, and the shop is the largest liquor shop in the Ningbo area. The following is the process of the discovery of tax evasion this time: The Ministry of Finance's Taxation Department noted that the collection of tobacco and alcohol taxes in the Ningbo factory was far less than the previous year's quota, so it specially sent Xiang Pi Zhen to Ningbo for thorough investigation. After arriving in Ningbo, the staff went to the Yin-Feng Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Branch Bureau to inquire about the reasons for the shortfall. The branch bureau replied that the market was sluggish and the business was depressed. Xiang then believed that although the sluggish market was one of the reasons for the shortfall, if the person responsible for collecting the taxes did not conduct a thorough inspection, the business community would arbitrarily evade donations and taxes, which was unavoidable. He then secretly investigated and discovered that the shop's production and sales volume were far different from the declared donation amount. The staff then handed over three copies of the shop's incoming and outgoing rolling stock book for the 25th year to the branch bureau for calculation. As a result, it was found that there had been tax evasion every year, and in the 25th year alone, there were 5,622 liters of private liquor, and 135 jars of private liquor were still being brewed and had not been taxed. It is reported that the shop will be punished in accordance with the regulations.

Page 9

Local News

Preserved Cultural Relics of the Forbidden City in Shanghai: The First Batch Was Shipped to Beijing Yesterday for Preservation; Special Trains Were Prepared to Stop at the Mackenzie Road Station for Loading; A Total of 3,151 Boxes Were All Porcelain, Bronze, and Jade Ware; The Rest Will Be Shipped Continuously; Military Police Will Protect the Trains 80

The cultural relics of the Palace Museum have been stored in the old site of Renji Hospital on Tiantang Street in the French Concession of Shanghai for three years. During this period, relevant agencies such as the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Education have sent personnel to open the boxes to inspect whether the various cultural relics are consistent with the storage list. However, due to the large number of items, the counting has not yet been completed. Now that the preservation warehouse building in Chaotian Palace, Nanjing has been completed, the Executive Yuan has approved the transportation of all the cultural relics stored in Shanghai to the warehouse in Beijing for preservation of the precious products of our country's past dynasties. The cultural relics in Shanghai include historical calligraphy and paintings, bronzes, porcelains, ancient books, jades, cloisonné enamel, lacquerware, silverware, rhinoceros horn ware, and silk tapestries. Most of them are precious products from the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties. Among the bronzes, there are many ancient objects from the Three Dynasties, which are particularly famous and rare. They are all packed in separate boxes, totaling more than 24,000 boxes.

Shipped Last Night

After receiving the order, Ouyang Banghua, director of the Shanghai Office of the Palace Museum, together with Shu Chushi, transport commissioner of the Ministry of Education, and various staff members of the office, went to the storage warehouse on Tiantang Street at 6 AM yesterday morning, opened the warehouse, inspected it, and then supervised the loading. The loading was handled by Mautai & Co., with a total of more than 40 loading trucks. Each time a box was moved out of the warehouse, the porters were given a token, and the staff registered it at the same time. It was not until 4:45 PM that it stopped. A total of 3,151 boxes of cultural relics were transported, including 76 boxes of the "Yi" character, 2,466 boxes of the "Hu" character, 189 boxes of the "Kan" character, and 420 boxes of the "Shang" character.

Strict Security

The special trains for transporting cultural relics consisted of 32 freight cars specially prepared by the Railway Bureau, parked at the Mackenzie Road Station. The station and its surroundings were guarded by police officers from the Public Security Bureau, soldiers from the Security Corps, together with military police and railway police. On the way from the warehouse to the Mackenzie Road Station, Chinese detectives from the French Concession Police Department were dispatched to protect the vehicles. A large number of Chinese and Western detectives were also stationed at the warehouse and Tiantang Street. They waited until 5 PM before withdrawing. The cultural relics special train left for Beijing at 11 PM last night. In addition to sending Xing Zhiliang and others to transport the cultural relics, the office also had military police, police officers, and railway police accompanying and protecting the train. According to the staff of the Shanghai Office of the Palace Museum, due to the large number of boxes of cultural relics stored in Shanghai, it was originally planned to transport 6,000 boxes first today (i.e., yesterday), but only 3,151 boxes could be transported. Among them were porcelain, bronzes, calligraphy, and paintings. The rest will continue to be shipped every three days.

Impact of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Detaining Rice Leads to Panic in Shanghai Grain Market; Representatives Sent to Zhenjiang Yesterday to Petition Jiangsu; Petition Submitted to Zhejiang to Expedite Release of Detained Rice 82

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Local Associations, Rice Merchants' Guild, Rice Grain Sales Guild, and Bean and Rice Trade Guild, due to the detention of rice shipments to Shanghai by Jiangsu's Jinshan, Qingpu, and other counties, as well as Zhejiang's Yongjia, Zhenhai, and other counties, has led to panic in the Shanghai grain market. Regarding Jiangsu Province, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Local Associations sent Gu Xinyi; the Bean and Rice Trade Guild sent Qiang Zisheng and Lu Jingwen; the Rice Merchants' Guild sent Lu Wenshao; and the Rice Grain Sales Guild's Rice Transport Merchants United Association sent Jiang Shizhi, a total of five people. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, they jointly took the 8:00 AM Nanjing-Shanghai express train to Zhenjiang to petition the Jiangsu Provincial Government's Department of Construction, Department of Finance, and Department of Civil Affairs, requesting them to comply with the Provisional Measures for Food Regulation of the Executive Yuan, to allow free domestic circulation, and to release the detained rice ships destined for Shanghai in order to maintain the food supply for Shanghai citizens. Regarding Zhejiang Province, a petition was submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: Regarding a petition matter, on the 7th of this month, a letter was received from the Miscellaneous Grains, Oil Cakes, and Related Industries Association, stating that the Yu Deqian Feng Company of the association had jointly ordered 9,700 bags of white rice from the Zhao Chunji Grain Store in Yongjia last month, which was purchased in Yueqing and Pingyang counties. A deposit of 20,000 yuan was paid immediately, with a one-month deadline for delivery. This rice has already been milled, but unexpectedly, the two counties suddenly prohibited its transportation. The small firms reported this to your association, and requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to provide a certificate for them to take to prove the situation, but it was still ineffective. Now, Zhao Chunji is pressing for the remaining payment, but the detained rice has not been released, and there is a risk of spoilage. The circulation of funds is greatly affected. Therefore, we are specially requesting your association to forward a petition to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, ordering Yueqing and Pingyang counties to release the detained white rice as soon as possible. Furthermore, the Da Cheng Company of the association stated that 5,000 shi of rice processed in Zhenhai were detained by the county. We also request that this case be included in the petition to order the county to release the rice. According to the above, the free domestic circulation of food has been decided by the central government. However, Yueqing, Pingyang, Zhenhai, and other counties in Zhejiang Province are obstructing the circulation of rice destined for Shanghai to provide food for the people. How can they obstruct circulation and defy laws and regulations? According to the previous situation, we dare not avoid bothering you with a letter requesting your association to investigate and verify the facts, and to prepare a document based on the facts to petition the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting them to instruct the relevant counties to release the rice purchased by Shanghai merchants immediately, in order to maintain government orders, which is a matter of public convenience. It was reported to the association that the Executive Yuan passed the Provisional Measures for Food Regulation on the 24th of last month, the first item of which states that food should be allowed to circulate freely within the country, and that the measures proposed by various provinces and cities to restrict the export of food are inconsistent with economic principles and the central government's principle of overall food management. All provinces and cities should immediately stop the ban on transportation. Now that rice from various counties in western Zhejiang is allowed to leave the province, Yueqing and Pingyang in southern Zhejiang, and Zhenhai in eastern Zhejiang, are still banning the export of rice, which is clearly inconsistent with the Executive Yuan's intention to stop the ban on transportation uniformly. Therefore, we have prepared a document to petition your government for review, requesting that you instruct the governments of each county to release the rice detained by Shanghai merchants immediately in order to maintain government orders, which is a matter of public convenience.

Japanese Shanghai Daily on Errors in Understanding China: Those Who View China with the Mindset of China Twenty or Thirty Years Ago and Consider Themselves China Experts Should Change Quickly 83

The Japanese Shanghai Daily published a commentary on the 7th of this month, titled "Understanding China! A Quick Change is Needed." An abridged translation of the main points is as follows:

Recently, the views of China held by so-called "China experts" in Japan are inevitably too outdated. Chinese newspapers often use the term "China expert" with sarcasm. The "China experts" in the so-called "view of China" are indeed something we should change. Why? In the past, our entry into China was based on views of China using terms such as "big country" and "sleeping lion." These terms have now become a thing of the past. Under the rule of the Nanjing government, China is now steadily advancing towards a modern unified nation. From the late Qing Dynasty to the early days of the revolution, the national situation was as chaotic as tangled hemp. Now, things are very different. However, if we introduce the progress of China, those who consider themselves China experts will immediately utter words of contempt for China, saying, "What does China have?" This kind of view is truly inappropriate. How can one hope to achieve cooperation and friendship by despising one's opponent? If one truly wants to cooperate and be friendly, one must recognize the position of the other country. Today, Japan is recognized by everyone as the leader of the East. However, despising the other country will only lead to being despised by the other country. The same is true for Japan's relationship with China. The "China view" of "China experts" is flaunted as the representative view of China in Japan, which is regrettable. The reason is that they are discussing China with the mindset of China twenty or thirty years ago, which is already very outdated. Any view of China that comes from the mouths of "China experts" and any negotiations conducted based on such views will hardly achieve any results. If you want to understand the situation in China, you cannot judge the merits and demerits of China based on the situation in major cities such as Nanjing, Beijing, Shanghai, and Guangzhou. Look at the personnel of the Nanjing government agencies. Whether it is the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, or the Ministry of Military Affairs, they can all report to work at 8:00 AM (7:30 AM in summer). This is very different from the public life of the Qing Dynasty and the early Republic of China. If Japan can be called "Young Japan," then China can be regarded as "Adolescent or Infant" China. China, which has established a central government in recent years, was originally in its infancy and is now moving from adolescence to youth. For example, today's Chinese youth, none of them smoke opium. Opium destroying the country is a story from the Qing Dynasty. Today's Chinese youth carry the nation on their backs, and the cry of opium destroying the country has long become a dream of the past. Today, no matter which country it is, its international relations are subject to a stronger influence than before, which is a major reason. Now, under the leadership of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, China is strengthening its unification, and the youth of the whole country have great faith in Chiang. This is the reality of China's progress. Therefore, if we desire Sino-Japanese cooperation, we must first quickly change Japan's understanding of China based on the aforementioned viewpoints and treat China with a new perspective. Only then can we expect Sino-Japanese cooperation.

Municipal and County Rice Industry Guilds Telegraphed the Executive Yuan 84

Request:

Lift the Ban on Rice Grain Exports; Do Not Allow Reduction or Exemption of Taxes on Foreign Rice

The Jiangsu Nanjing-Shanghai Municipal and County Rice Industry Guilds, due to news reports that the Guangdong Provincial Government has telegraphed the central government to exempt taxes on imported foreign rice, stated that if this is approved, it would not only affect the rural economy but also lead to the outflow of rights and interests. Therefore, yesterday, they telegraphed the Executive Yuan, requesting that it not be approved, and further requesting that it order all provinces to quickly lift the ban on rice exports to facilitate domestic circulation. The original telegram is recorded below: To Premier Chiang of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing: We have found that the provincial governments, in order to prevent smuggling to the sea, have banned the export of rice grains, which has caused panic among the people in rice-deficient provinces. After repeated appeals from our associations, we were fortunate to have your approval not to do so. However, obstruction under various pretexts is still heard from time to time. The most serious case is that of Jiading County detaining rice ships destined for Shanghai, which has not yet been resolved. If the ban by this province is not lifted, then surpluses cannot make up for shortages, and mutual circulation is not possible. Therefore, the Guangdong Provincial Government has submitted a request to the central government to reduce or exempt taxes on imported foreign rice, which has been announced in the newspapers, causing widespread consternation. We have found that the taxation of foreign rice was originally intended to prevent the outflow of rights and interests and to protect farmers. Although Guangdong Province feels a shortage of rice, rice-producing areas can circulate and supply it. Moreover, with the Guangdong-Hankou Railway open, it is no longer difficult to transport from rice-producing provinces in the Yangtze River basin. In addition, this year's grain harvest is abundant everywhere, and the rural economy is expected to recover. Instead of procuring foreign rice, which would lead to the outflow of money, it would be better to purchase it from various provinces to retain rights and interests. If the province's request is approved, the rural economy of Jiangsu and Zhejiang will inevitably be affected, and sales in rice-producing provinces will stagnate. This would be contrary to the central government's intention to manage food overall. Our associations feel a sense of danger and cannot remain silent. We dare to telegram your leader for review, hoping that you will order all provinces to quickly lift the ban on rice exports, and that the Guangdong Province's request to exempt taxes on imported foreign rice will not be approved, in order to protect farmers and merchants. We would be endlessly grateful. Gu Xinyi, Standing Chairman; Zhao Zixin, Zhu Zixiang, Yin Zhongren, and Pang Qinsheng, Standing Committee Members, of the Joint Association of Rice Industry Guilds of Jiangsu Nanjing-Shanghai Municipal and County, respectfully kowtow. Another 50,000 yuan was remitted to the central government.

Huang Fu's Remains Embalmed Yesterday; Simple and Solemn Arrangement of the Hall; Chiang Sent His Wife as Representative to Pay Respects; Yan Xishan and Others Sent Condolence Telegrams 86

The remains of National Government Committee Member Huang Fu were embalmed at 3:00 PM yesterday at the China Funeral Home on Haig Road. The arrangement of the hall was generally simple, and wreaths and couplets were not hung or displayed. Madam Zhu Meiling, representing Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Vice President of the Executive Yuan Kong Xiangxi, and people from all walks of life, both Chinese and foreign, who knew Huang during his lifetime, went to pay their respects, reaching 500 to 600 people. The plain cars and white horses crowded Haig Road. The coffin is temporarily kept in the funeral home and will be transported for burial after the burial site is determined. The details are recorded below:

Condolences from Relatives and Friends

Huang had extensive social connections during his lifetime. At the embalming, 500 to 600 people went to pay their respects before the spirit and to look at the remains. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek was unable to attend in person due to busy official duties, so he sent his wife, Madam Song Meiling, as a representative to pay respects. In addition, those who attended included Vice President of the Executive Yuan Kong Xiangxi and his wife, Chu Minyi representing the Chairman of the Central Political Council, President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke, Yang Hu representing Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin, Minister of Communications Yu Feipeng, Tang Guozhen representing Deputy Commander of the Northwest Bandit Suppression Zhang Xueliang, Deng Gang representing Guangdong Pacification Director Yu Hanmou and Xiang Hanping, Tao Luqian, head of the Ministry of Interior Affairs, Wang Shina representing Ambassador to Japan Xu Shiying, Ambassador to the United States Wang Zhengting, Minister to Turkey He Yaozu, Xu Qingfu, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of this city, Yang Hu, Commander of the Songhu Garrison, Zhou Jue, Director of the Foreign Affairs Office, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, Xue Dubi, Zou Lu and Madam Zou representing him, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, Zhou Xiangxian, Mayor of Hangzhou, Xie Zhongfu, Member of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government of this city, Cai Jingjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Public Works Bureau, Shen Yi, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Finance, Chen Taoyi, Secretary-General of the Municipal Council, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Roads Bureau, as well as Xu Xiuzhi, Qian Xinzhi, Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Yu Zuoting, Yuan Ludeng, Zhou Zuomin, Ye Gongchuo, Yang Dezhao, Yin Tong, Tao Baichuan, Yuan Liang, Li Zeyi, and the Huang clan, among others. The consuls general stationed in Shanghai who attended included U.S. Consul General Gauss, French Consul General Baudat, German Consul General Kriebel, Japanese Consul General Wakasugi, Italian Consul General Nilon, and many others, including Japanese Naval Attaché Sato.

Order of Embalming

The arrangement of the hall was simple and solemn. On both sides were military bands from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters and the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Only Huang's portrait was hung in front of the spirit, and fresh flowers and fruits were offered on the table. Other elegiac couplets and wreaths were not hung or displayed in accordance with his will. The order of the embalming was also very simple, including: (1) Family members paying respects; (2) Clan members paying respects; (3) Relatives and friends paying respects; (4) Public memorial service. The order of the public memorial service included: (1) All standing in silence; (2) Playing mourning music; (3) Burning incense and playing music; (4) Reading the memorial text; (5) Bowing three times; (6) Conclusion of the ceremony.

Viewing the Remains

Chinese and foreign people from all walks of life went to the China Funeral Home to pay their respects successively from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM yesterday. After paying their respects, they formed a line and walked to the back of the spirit tent to view the remains. Madam Huang and her family stood around the coffin with their heads bowed and tears streaming down their faces. Huang had believed that the complicated customs of weddings and funerals needed to be improved. In his will, he stated that the funeral must be simple, that all frivolous rituals should be eliminated, and that there was no need to wail loudly by the coffin. Therefore, the funeral was extremely simple and solemn. The coffin was made of Phoebe nanmu. Huang's embalming clothes were also in accordance with his will, wearing a domestically produced blue robe and black jacket. Huang's remains were very thin due to years of serious illness. His coffin will be temporarily kept in the China Funeral Home and will be transported for burial after the burial site is determined.

Labor Service Committee Held District Talks Yesterday; Reported the Significance of Service and Instructed on the Progress of Projects; District Propaganda Was Held Yesterday in Jiangwan Yinxiang 87

The Shanghai Municipal Labor Service Committee held talks with district directors and map directors at the committee's office in the Municipal Central District Aviation Association yesterday afternoon to discuss progress. As for district officials' reports, they were held in the Jiangwan and Yinxiang districts yesterday. The details of each item are recorded below:

Instructions on Projects

Yesterday's talks were attended by over 100 people, including Hong Qi, Chief Organizer of the Labor Service Committee, Deputy Chief Organizers Xu Guansan and Wu Huanru, Organizers Dai Erjing and Yu Zhenhui, and district directors. This meeting is being convened to hope that everyone will express their great opinions and jointly plan the progress, so that the service can begin and be completed as soon as possible. Deputy Chief Organizer Xu Guansan will explain the service outline and various laws in detail, hoping that everyone will work hard to promote them. After the report, district directors Yang Xinzheng, Pan Hongding, Hong Lanxiang, and Zhu Jiajun successively expressed their opinions on various aspects of the progress, such as the difference between the police district and the administrative district, the need to re-divide the household registration, and the student service issue, which were discussed in detail.

District Propaganda

Yesterday's district propaganda was held in the Jiangwan and Yinxiang districts, with Deputy Chief Organizer Wu Huanru and Organizer Yu Zhenhui of the Service Committee giving guidance. In Jiangwan, it was held at the Municipal Committee Office, with over 50 representatives from various circles attending. Chairman Gu Shanzhang appointed the Seventh District Party Headquarters Municipal Committee Office, Xikou Elementary School, and Lida Academy to be responsible for the propaganda. In Yinxiang District, it was held at the Yinbei Elementary School on Mayushan Road, with over 40 representatives from various circles attending. Chairman Li Zhuohong decided to engage in propaganda starting today to ensure that every household knows about it. Tomorrow's district propaganda will be held in the Zhenru District at 10:00 AM at the Zhenru Town Municipal Committee Office, and in the Pusong District at 2:00 PM inside the Pusong Town Defense Corps. It is also heard that the Yangsi and Tangqiao districts have also requested to hold labor services.

###瓯海 Customs Superintendent Xu Hongbin Arrives in Shanghai for Talks

Smuggling at the Ou Customs Eliminated; Tax Revenue Increases Fourfold

Ou Customs Superintendent Xu Hongbin arrived in Shanghai from Wenzhou yesterday to pay respects to the late National Government Committee member Huang Fu. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency interviewed Mr. Xu, who said that the Ou Customs had previously been greatly affected by smuggling by Japanese and Taiwanese residents. After assuming his post, he immediately followed the instructions of the authorities and made every effort to crack down on it. Now the smuggling trend has been completely eliminated, and tax revenue has increased fourfold compared to before. Mr. Xu will visit Finance Minister Kong in the coming days to report.

Chiang Ting-wen and Xiang Hanping Fly to Shaanxi and Guangdong Yesterday Morning 88

Chiang Ting-wen, Director of Pacification of Fujian, arrived in Shanghai from Fujian a few days ago. Yesterday morning at 6:30, he took a Eurasia Aviation Corporation plane and flew to Shaanxi in a hurry.

Mr. Xiang Hanping, Deputy Commander of the Fourth Route Army, flew south to Guangdong on a China National Aviation Corporation Shanghai-Guangdong flight yesterday morning.

Yu Feipeng Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 89

Minister of Transportation Yu Feipeng left Nanjing by night train the night before last at 11:00 PM and arrived in Shanghai at around 7:00 AM yesterday morning. Mr. Yu's visit is for official business, and he is scheduled to stay in Shanghai briefly before returning to Nanjing.

North Sichuan Road Police Station Searches for Drugs in Private Homes; Sends Police Chiefs in Groups to Search; Detains Thirty-Nine Male and Female Suspects 90

The North Sichuan Road Police Station, under orders to strictly prohibit drugs, specially sent Police Chief Meng Jinmin and others, in three groups of over forty police chiefs, to conduct intensive searches from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM yesterday in Fengsheng Lane, Washington Lane, Caopeng of Xin Jia Road, Qiujiang Road, Changchun Road, Taikang Lane, Shunxing Lane, and other locations within their jurisdiction. As a result, they arrested a large number of morphine and red pill users, including Pan Fu, Zhao Zigui, Ding Wanchun, and thirty-seven others, as well as two female suspects. Together with the drugs and drug paraphernalia seized, they were taken to the station for interrogation and then transferred to the Songhu Garrison Command for investigation at 6:00 PM in the afternoon.

Li Hongwen Travels North to Report Back Yesterday Evening 91

It is reported that after a short stay in Beijing, he will return to Shanxi to report back.

Women's Association to Aid Suiyuan Holds Fundraising Group Meeting Yesterday 92

The fundraising group of the Women's Association for Comforting Soldiers in Suiyuan held a meeting at the YWCA on Jing'an Temple Road yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Yan Yaqing, Wu Daiyi, Xie Zuyi, Chen Yongshang, Pu Mansong, Shen Ziju, Tang Guanyu, and representatives from Shanghai Taozhong and other schools in Nanyang, totaling more than twenty people, attended. Xie Zuyi presided over the meeting. The following resolutions were made: (1) To notify all sectors of society who have pledged donations to send their clothing to the receiving agencies as soon as possible; (2) To schedule a date for inviting women to solicit donations separately; (3) To have the directors of this group solicit donations from their relatives and friends. The association issued a notice stating: "To whom it may concern, recently, bandits have invaded the border areas, and puppet troops have been wreaking havoc. The international situation is becoming increasingly tense. The soldiers on the front lines are enduring great hardships. Our association is taking the lead in fundraising for comfort. If people from all walks of life would like to donate money or goods, please deliver them directly to the following agencies, which will issue receipts with the seal of this association and the name of the executive director Wang Xiaoying as proof. This matter concerns a charitable cause of comforting the soldiers. We hope that all sectors will actively contribute. This notice is hereby given. Current cash receiving locations: Head office and branches of the Bank of China, head office and branches of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Women's Bank on Nanjing Road, Room 415, 4th Floor, Central Building on Edward Road. Receiving locations for goods: This association, Zhonghua Vocational School on Yingxun Road, Lujiabang, YWCA on Jing'an Temple Road, China Women's Middle School on Lin Yin Road, West Gate, and China Vocational Education Society on Hualong Road."

Representatives from Various Police Stations Discuss Salary Cut Plan 93

According to the Continental News, representatives from various police stations in the Public Concession met with Chief Inspector of the Police Department Qiu Laide at the Chief Inspector's Office on Fuzhou Road on Sunday afternoon to discuss the terms of the special economic committee report passed by the Municipal Council. Two police officers from each police station attended, representing the staff of their respective police stations, to express their opinions on the report's proposal to reduce staff salaries by 80 percent and various allowances. The Chief Inspector then explained the report to the representatives. After a brief discussion, the meeting adjourned. It is reported that the Chief Inspector will compile the opinions of all members on the salary reduction and submit a report to the Municipal Council.

National Church Jointly Manages War Zone Relief Affairs; Cheng Jingyi Reports on the Current Situation in Suiyuan; Zhao Jinqing Exhorts Church Members to Contribute 96

Cheng Jingyi, General Secretary of the National General Assembly of the Chinese Christian Church in Beiping, came to Shanghai. Zhao Jinqing, Chairman of the War Zone Relief Committee of the Shanghai Christian Association, held a banquet at the Western Restaurant of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at noon yesterday. Wang Wanbai, Huang Hanxin, Lu Ganchen, and twenty other people attended. Zhao Jinqing delivered a welcoming speech. Then, Cheng Jingyi reported that when he left Beiping, according to the report of the Suiyuan War Zone Inspection Team, Pastors Zhang and Gao, after inspecting the Suiyuan War Zone, made the following decisions on the spot: (1) Request the National Christian Council to select the National Church to jointly manage war zone relief efforts; (2) Plead for the people in the war zone: (1) The compatriots in the Suiyuan War Zone are either freezing and starving to death, or dying from gunshot wounds, or even sitting and waiting to die. Can we bear not to save them? (2) We have always said that we love Jesus, love the country, and love our compatriots. Now is the opportunity to put our love into practice. (3) "If anyone does not love his brother, whom he has seen, he cannot love God, whom he has not seen." (4) "Truly I tell you, whatever you did for one of the least of these brothers and sisters of mine, you did for me." (5) Love is not just lip service; it is about practical action. Relieving compatriots in the war zone is serving God. (3) The letter to the national church members is as follows: "Respected Sir/Madam, The bandit-puppet invasion of Suiyuan has aroused public outrage around the world. In view of the fact that the compatriots in the war zone have suffered greatly from the war and the soldiers on the front lines are loyally defending the country, our association has specially organized the War Zone Relief Committee to raise emergency relief funds. We have entrusted Cheng Jingyi, General Secretary of the National General Assembly of the Chinese Christian Church in Beiping, and Professor Mei Yibao of Yenching University to investigate the needs of the disaster areas nearby in order to raise funds. Now, the military and civilians are in urgent need of relief. They are not sure they can even last the day. Therefore, we urgently appeal and seek relief. We hope that the believers of each church will have the heart of Christ's compassion for the world, sympathize with the compatriots who have suffered, pay attention to saving food and clothing, economize on entertainment, and actively contribute and work hard to raise funds. The first phase is scheduled to end at the end of this year. For any items, please hand them over to the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA for forwarding. If it is a donation, you can entrust it to your church pastor to deposit it, or directly entrust it in the name of our association to the Bank of China on Sanma Road Bund, Zhejiang Industrial Bank on Beijing Road, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank Branch on Eight Immortals Bridge, or Jincheng Bank Branch on Eight Immortals Bridge to remit it to the war zone for relief. This matter concerns the survival of the nation and the life and death of our compatriots. All of us believers must do our best to fulfill our great duty. Sincerely requesting peace. Zhao Jinqing, President."

Cotton Order Breach of Contract Litigation 97

You Ju-sun sues Gui Yan-fang

Shouji Company, Yu Jusun, purchased 112,000 dan of Shanghai Chinese Cloth Exchange standard cotton for July from Tongji Company on July 9th of this year. A contract was signed, stating that the price per dan was 45.40 yuan, with delivery at the end of the month. Shouji paid a deposit of 150,000 yuan. If either party violated the contract, a penalty of double the deposit amount would be imposed. Later, due to circumstances, the contract could not be fulfilled on time, so the contract was revised to extend the period by one month. However, when the deadline arrived, the seller still did not send samples, so it was not possible to ship the goods to him. It was not until September that the seller delivered part of the goods. Upon inspection, it was discovered that the quality of the 64,700 bales of cotton stored in the warehouse was very poor and significantly different from the original sample. The buyer requested the seller to terminate the contract, return the deposit, and compensate for the losses. After a long negotiation, no agreement could be reached. Therefore, Yun Jusun hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to file a lawsuit against Tongji Gui Yanfang in the First Special District Court, requesting a judgment to repay the deposit of 150,000 yuan, the warehouse and insurance fees of 50,000 yuan, the breach of contract penalty of 300,000 yuan, and the annual interest of 5% on each item, as well as litigation costs. After several hearings, no conclusion was reached. Yesterday morning, the Civil Court President Li Hu specially convened a collegiate bench to summon both parties and the giant of the silk and cotton industry, Shen Changgeng, to the case for interrogation. Since further investigation was still needed, it was ordered to postpone the hearing to another date.

Details of the Derailment of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Train the Day Before Yesterday 98

A freight train that departed from Beijing on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway the morning before yesterday derailed between Wuxi Zhoujingxiang Station, causing the Beijing-Kai express train to be delayed. This was briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now, news has come from the bureau that differs slightly from what was reported yesterday. Therefore, it is continued as follows: On the morning of the 7th, freight train No. 505 departed from Beijing. At 4:17 pm, after departing from Wuxi Station, when it reached the 118-kilometer mark between Wuxi and Zhoujingxiang Stations, the axle of the fifth carriage, the Jiangnan Railway freight car No. 2642, suddenly broke, causing the entire train to be unable to move. After receiving the report, the Zhoujingxiang Station Master urgently reported to the Wuxi Station officials, who dispatched the Beijing-Kai midday express train locomotive that had arrived at the station to the scene of the accident to tow the rear carriages of the freight train back to Wuxi Station. The front carriages were taken to Zhoujingxiang Station by the freight train locomotive. The broken axle car was urgently dispatched from Wujin Station with a rescue car and a crane to attempt rescue. Because it was late at night and there was rain and snow, the work was difficult. It was not until 11 pm that it was hoisted and moved off the track. At that time, the special express train that departed from Nanjing at 5 pm had also arrived at Wuxi Station after the midday express train. It was ordered to merge and depart from Wuxi, according to the special express train schedule, a delay of two hours and forty-four minutes. Along the way, because there were more cars attached, the journey was inevitably slow. When it reached Anting, there was a slight delay due to the removal of the broken hook car, so it arrived in Shanghai at 3:07 am on the 8th, a delay of four hours and seventeen minutes, six hours later than the arrival time of the midday express train. The reason for the Jiangnan car's axle breakage is currently being investigated by the railway.

Two Firefighters Injured on Duty by Public Concession Decides to Compensate 100

Two firefighters, No. 59 and No. 49, of the Public Concession Fire Brigade were injured on duty, resulting in disability and inability to continue service. The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession, after receiving a request from the Shaoxing Seven Counties Association for negotiation, repeatedly requested compensation from the Public Concession Bureau to uphold humanity. The association received a reply from the Public Concession Bureau yesterday, stating: "I have received your letters of September 23 and November 17. Regarding the case of firefighters No. 59 and No. 49 being injured on duty, this bureau has re-examined the case. It has now been decided to retain the two officers in the team until the end of the year. At that time, they will be retired due to illness and disability, and in addition to the savings they are entitled to, they will be given compensation equal to one and a half years' salary."

Record of the Second Regular Meeting of the Chinese Institute of Mining and Metallurgical Engineering 105

Engineer Rafalusin Reports on the Situation in Hainan Island

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Institute of Mining and Metallurgical Engineering held its second regular meeting at the Wuzhou Building at 6 pm on the 6th of this month. President Lu Zhixue announced the opening of the meeting. First, the secretary read the minutes of the previous meeting, which were approved by the members. Then, the chairman introduced Mr. Rafalusin, former engineer of the Muling Coal Mine and current consultant engineer of the Dutch Silver Company, to the colleagues. Mr. Rafalusin summarized the mining survey of Hainan Island, Guangdong Province, and used diagrams and photographs to illustrate. The survey was conducted by Mr. Rafalusin, accompanied by a Chinese geologist and an American miner. The entire process took 82 days, covering a distance of 603 kilometers on foot and by measurement, 60 kilometers on horseback, and 1,260 kilometers by car. The area surveyed in detail was 200 square kilometers, the area inspected was 900 square kilometers, and the area investigated was 1,200 square kilometers. Hainan Island is located between 18 and 20 degrees north latitude and 108 degrees 30 minutes to 111 degrees east longitude. The total population is 400,000. The main seaport is called Haikou, which is 460 kilometers from Hong Kong. The original report was very detailed and interesting. An excerpt of the original text is as follows: In southern Hainan Island, the summer climate is often above 100 degrees Fahrenheit, with an average between 80 and 97 degrees. In July, August, and September, there is heavy rain almost every day. The island's plants have been studied by students of Lingnan University and Chinese and foreign scientists. The most common diseases are malaria and hookworm disease. 85% of the rural population suffers from hookworm disease, and the incidence of malaria is similar. Medical treatment is provided by municipal and American Presbyterian hospitals. Agricultural products include rice, beans, peanuts, sesame seeds, and indigo. Oak, lacquer, sugarcane, pineapple, coffee, cocoa, etc. are all cultivated, but animals are not very reproductive. Three years ago, tin mines were opened in northern Hainan Island. As of September of this year, a total of 270 tons of tin have been produced. There are still about 430 tons of reserves in the same area. It can be seen that the scale of tin mining is not large, but the benefits are still good. The survey team regretted that it could not complete the survey of the central part of the island. According to the report of the Industrial and Commercial Survey Team, in addition to tin mines, there are also outcrops of gold, antimony, lead, sulfur, iron, and copper mines, but they have not been tested and their commercial value is unknown. At 8 pm, there was a dinner. During the dinner, Mr. Cheng Zhongshi, Director of the Mining Bureau, gave a speech on the future trend of China's mining industry and the improvement of government agency administration, explaining that Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry hopes that government agencies will be commercialized to increase efficiency. Director Cheng has been serving in the mining industry for more than 20 years and is well aware of the difficulties of mining merchants. Now that he is the administrative officer, he should be able to solve all the difficulties for mining merchants and benefit the mining industry immensely. Those who attended the meeting that day included Li Zushen, Liu Hongsheng, Cheng Zhongshi, Yu Heyin, Yu Gengshi, Yang Yunyan, Cai Renfu, Gu Zhiyun, Su Jianxun, Rafalusin, Yi Chaogeng, Pan Taomin, Shen Maiqun, Lu Zhixue, Sun Xianhui, Qu Lianke, Zheng Weisan, Guo Chengen, Kang Shiqing, Yu Mingyu, Fang Zizhong, Wang Shengsan, Shen Yuanru, and others, a total of 23 people. The meeting ended happily at 9:30 pm. It is said that the cost of the dinner was borne by Wang Ziven, Yu Ziwei, and Sun Deqing.

The Second Special Court Continues to Hear the Case of Gu Zhuxuan Each Person Firmly Denies Inciting to Recant Zhao Guangfu's Testimony is Irrelevant The Case Still Needs to be Investigated and Continued to Another Date 108

Gu Zhuxuan from Yancheng, the former owner of the Quanchan Stage, was arrested for being suspected of inciting murder in the Tang Jiapeng assassination case. During the period when the Second High Court of Appeal was hearing the case and scheduling a sentencing date, Gu bribed Wu Lu, the head of the guard sent by the Second Special Court's detention center to the Guangci Hospital's external prison ward, and the guard Ma Xianxiang, who in turn entrusted Wang Yushou, the head of the guard of the Second Special Prison, and the guards Ma Xianxiang, Ma Xiancai, Wang Bogang, etc., to buy off the prisoners Zhao Guangfu and Zhang Yangui (also known as Xiao Sizi) to recant their testimony and acquit him. After the case was revealed, the Ma Xianxiang and Ma Xiancai brothers, Wang Yushou, Wang Bogang, etc., abandoned their posts and fled. Wu Lu and Ma Xianxiang were detained. After the prosecutor Wang Ren of the Second Special Court checked with the Daya Bank and confirmed that there was a deposit of 2,000 yuan under the name of Zhang Sen, after investigation, Gu's brother Gu Songmao was also suspected. Therefore, Gu Zhuxuan, Gu Songmao, Wu Lu, Ma Xianxiang, etc. were publicly prosecuted by the prosecutor in the Criminal Court of the same court on charges of inciting to recant and dereliction of duty. At the same time, an order was issued to arrest the escaped guards, the Ma brothers and the two Wangs, in the case. The public prosecution case has been tried several times without a conclusion. Now, Judge Chen Shuoying has taken over the case and opened a new trial, scheduling another hearing at a later date. All the circumstances have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 2:45 pm, Judge Chen, together with Prosecutor Wang, continued the trial of the defendants in the Second Criminal Court. The defense lawyers selected by the defendants, Jiang Yiping, Cao Shoulin, Gao Wenqi, etc., also arrived on time to await instructions. The court first summoned the defendant Ma Xianxiang, 24 years old, from Anhui. In April of the 22nd year, Judge Xiong introduced him to the detention center of this court as a guard. Although the guards Ma Xianxiang and Ma Xiancai in the prison were his uncles, they did not interact with each other. This time in Shanghai, he only got to know them after his uncle mentioned it. Their duties were different, and they did not often meet and talk. Wu Lu was the head guard in the detention center. I did not worship him as a teacher. He was in the external prison ward, and I served in this office. We did not often talk, and Wu did not entrust me with any matters. Regarding Gu Zhuxuan's case, no one entrusted me to contact Ma Xianxiang to contact the prisoners to recant their testimony. Gu was in the external prison ward, and I was in this office. I have not met Gu, nor have I discussed anything with Gu's family. This is absolutely unjust. After a few months of litigation, I went home after being released on bail. I went to Ma Xianxiang's house to look for him, but he said he had not returned home. I did not know about Gu Zhuxuan's instigation to recant before. I did not know it until the prosecutor asked me when I was detained. I have not wronged Gu. If I had really done this, they would have all run away, and I would not have stayed here to eat litigation. When I was detained, I was still serving. The official said to Ma, according to Zhang Tinggui's confession, Ma Xianxiang said to him that Gu Zhuxuan entrusted Wu Zhongren to entrust you, and then entrusted Ma Xianxiang to contact Zhang. Do you admit this? If Zhang could not go out of the prison, how could he know so much in detail and say that you were involved? There must be a reason. Ma replied that they were talking nonsense. What evidence is there? At this point, Zhang Tinggui was brought to the case. He was asked if he knew Ma. Zhang replied that he did not know him. He asked Ma again, do you know Zhao Guangfu? He replied that he had guarded Zhao before, so he knew him. The official ordered Zhang to confess again how Ma Xianxiang contacted him to recant his testimony (the wording is the same as recorded in the previous newspaper). Ma still flatly denied that this had happened. Zhao Guangfu was then brought to the case and interrogated about the process of contacting him to recant his testimony in prison. Zhao's testimony was flickering and irrelevant, and it seemed quite ridiculous. The official questioned his previous confession and ordered him to confess again. Zhao said that many days had passed, and he had forgotten. Please check the files. The official then ordered Wu Lu to be brought to the case. Wu cried out for injustice and denied that he had been entrusted by Gu Zhuxuan to ask Ma Xianxiang to entrust him to recant his testimony. He also denied that he had been to Gu's house. He also claimed that there was another director surnamed He in the detention center who was a local and whose accent could not be distinguished from Wu. He asked for a detailed investigation. If there was any connection, he was willing to accept the punishment. At this point, Gu Songmao was brought to the case and interrogated about the deposit in the Daya Bank. He replied that he did not know. He asked, according to Zhang Tinggui's confession, Ma Xianxiang and you and Zheng Jianer went to the bank to deposit the money? He replied, please investigate again. If I went to deposit the money, then I cannot deny it. He asked, Gu Zhuxuan is your younger brother. You should find a way for him. If you deny it, is it possible that there are such good people outside who will pay to help your brother? He replied, I really did not go to deposit the money. There are many backgrounds to this case. There are anonymous letters to the court and the lawyers we hired, and Guo Tang Wu Mei, etc., which have been identified by the Third High Prosecutor as having the same handwriting. Please investigate secretly to extend the injustice. Since my brother was arrested, in addition to hiring lawyers to provide legal assistance, although someone called and asked to contact me, some did not say their names, and some set a location to find no one. Finally, Gu Zhuxuan was brought to the case and asked, Gu, you have been asked several times, and you have all denied it, but the bank deposit is real. He replied, I was in the external prison ward with someone guarding me and never left. I did not ask anyone to do it. I don't know who went to deposit this money inside. The Third High Court acquitted me. The verdict did not adopt the recanted words of Zhao and Zhang, but adopted the various evidence presented by my lawyer. I did not commit a crime. I would rather fight a lawsuit than buy their words. If I had listened to them, they would have only wanted a few hundred yuan from me at the beginning. I did not listen to them because there was no such thing. How could I then spend a huge amount of money to buy them? After the questioning, the court believed that the case still needed investigation and could not be closed. Therefore, it announced that it would be heard again at a later date. Gu Songmao and Ma Xianxiang were still released on bail, and the remaining people were still remanded in custody.

Hengli River Has Been Dredged 109

Shanghai County's dredging of the Hengli River began on the 5th of this month with the construction of a dam. Yesterday, the flow was cut off. Qi Kezhong, the technical director of the county government, together with Zhang Fengshan, the head of the third district, and Wu Shifang, the head of the first district, hired a small boat yesterday to inspect the dam work. The river has not been repaired for 47 years, and the project is huge. The Puji Nursing Home has a water pavilion, and the water source is taken from Hengli. Therefore, two wooden river dams will be temporarily built in that section, and the construction of the Xiyin Port dam will be slowed down to provide for other projects. When the project is completed, it will be reduced and dredged again. The first and third district offices are now preparing for the lottery procedures. It will be divided into sections on the 10th, and excavation can begin on the 12th. As for the water lifting project, bidding has been open for many days, and there are many enthusiastic bidders. The bidding will be opened publicly in the county government auditorium at 1 pm tomorrow.

Municipal North and North Shanghai Health Centers to Open 110

New Building Completed, Opening Date Selected

The Shanghai Municipal Government considers health matters of utmost importance to the health of the nation. Passively, it can eliminate epidemics and reduce mortality, while actively, it can extend life and increase production. Therefore, it has established health centers in various districts to plan public health. Centers have already been established in Gaoqiao, Wusong, Jiangwan, and South Shanghai. However, the Zhabei area has been in poor sanitary condition since the January 28th Incident. Given the large population, it is necessary to establish a health institution. Mayor Wu, concerned about the health of the citizens, allocated 50,000 yuan from the municipal treasury to order Li Ting'an, the Director of the Health Bureau, to promptly establish a North Shanghai Health Center to protect the health of the citizens. After engaging Wang Binyan, Chen Bingqian, Wang Yunwu, Wang Peiyuan, Shen Yi, Lu Bohong, and Li Ting'an as preparation committee members, a site was selected on Qingyun Road in Zhabei, and construction began last spring. It is now completed. The health center is scheduled to open on November 1st. In addition to all administrative affairs, it will handle diagnosis and treatment, street cleaning and disinfection, maternal and child health, and infectious disease prevention. Impoverished citizens who seek medical treatment will receive free medication. There are also plans to establish public bathhouses to benefit the public. Once the entire center is completely organized, a formal opening ceremony will be held.

Pharmacists Association Held General Meeting Yesterday 111

Proposals Passed and Officers Re-elected

The Shanghai Pharmacists Association held its third general meeting at its clubhouse on Tongfu Road yesterday. Dozens of members, including Zhou Mengbai, attended. Qiu Shaobai, Cao Zhigong, and Shen Zhongmou served as the presidium, with Wang Fushen as the recorder. After the meeting commenced, Qiu Shaobai delivered the opening address. Cao Zhigong then reported on association affairs, and Shen Zhongmou reported on financial matters. Subsequently, Mao Yun, representing the municipal party headquarters, and Lei Kenan, representing the Social Affairs Bureau, delivered speeches of encouragement. The following proposals were then discussed: (1) increasing the number of executive committee members; (2) requesting the central government to facilitate the organization of the Pharmacists Association before the promulgation of the Pharmacists Association Law; (3) requesting the central government to promptly promulgate the Pharmacist Law and the Pharmacists Association Law; (4) requesting the Ministry of Health to revise the text of Article 24 of the Provisional Pharmacist Regulations; (6) requesting the Ministry of Health to promulgate regulations for the manufacture and transportation of narcotics; (7) formulating a pharmacist's creed; (8) requesting the central government that pharmaceutical matters related to medicine and health should be handled primarily by pharmaceutical personnel; (9) requesting the Ministry of Health to promptly formulate the second edition of the Chinese Pharmacopoeia; (10) requesting the Ministry of Education to order the National Institute for Compilation and Translation to revise pharmaceutical terminology. All of the above proposals were passed. It was then decided to hold a vote for the election.
