Real Estate Market Decline: Millionaire Becomes Impoverished, All Properties Sealed, Even Residence Cannot Be Preserved 112

Yang Qingsheng, a local resident and manager of Puyi Real Estate Company, who lived in the Fahua Town west of Shanghai for three years, previously had assets worth nearly ten million yuan. Two New Vessels Purchased by Sanbei Company Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday 116

Suitable for Both Flood and Shallow Waters

Due to the improvement of the Yangtze River shipping industry this year, the Sanbei Company found that its original vessels were insufficient to meet demand. Furthermore, as the river level fell, ships with deeper drafts were obstructed. Therefore, the company purchased one Longshan and one Ruian vessel from Hong Kong and Macau Steamboat Company. Another large vessel was also purchased. After the vessels were purchased, Xie Shunmao, Assistant Manager, and Pao Shi, Chief Captain, along with all 86 crew members, were sent to Hong Kong on the 11th of last month to bring the two new vessels to Shanghai. The Longshan was renamed Longxing, and the Ruian was renamed Long'an. Xie Shunmao has transferred to the Yuehan Railway to inspect the Yangtze River shipping industry in Hunan. Pao Shi led the two new vessels from Hong Kong to Shanghai. Yesterday morning, the Longxing arrived in Shanghai first. The Long'an had to wait until night to reach Wusong and will enter the port this morning. Both vessels have a carrying capacity of 1,500 tons each, and their construction is excellent. They were both completed in 1935, have shallow drafts, and have a large cargo capacity and excellent passenger accommodations. They are most suitable for the Yangtze River and can travel in both flood and shallow waters. Upon arrival in Shanghai, the two vessels will be driven to the Sanbei Machinery Factory for repairs. At the same time, they will be reported to the Maritime Affairs Bureau for registration, obtain navigation licenses, and change the national flag. As soon as the work is completed, they will be assigned to the Yangtze River to operate.

Zhejiang Silk Control Association Borrows Money to Improve Silk Cocoons 117

According to Xin Xin News Agency, in order to meet the needs of various regions and develop the silk industry, the Zhejiang Silk Control Association has decided to purchase more spring silkworm seeds and distribute them to various breeding areas. However, the domestic production of spring silkworm seeds in recent years has been insufficient to supply all regions. Therefore, the association has borrowed 400,000 yuan from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications to order 800,000 sheets of spring silkworm seeds from abroad to supplement the shortage. The price per sheet is 0.75 yuan, totaling 600,000 yuan. In addition to borrowing 400,000 yuan from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, the remaining 200,000 yuan will be supplemented from the profits of selling spring silkworm silk this year. The seed purchase loan contract has been signed, with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications each providing 200,000 yuan at an interest rate of 9%, with the purchased silkworm seeds as collateral, and stipulates that the principal and interest will be repaid in full when the spring cocoons are put on the market next year.

Improving Cocoon-Drying Equipment in Cocoon Shops

The association has recognized that the improved varieties of cocoons raised in recent years are of good quality. In order to further improve and increase production, it has decided to improve the old-fashioned cocoon stoves in various cocoon shops and uniformly adopt new-style cooperative cocoon dryers to save manpower and time. It has agreed with the Bank of China to borrow 600,000 yuan to order 20 new machines and order various cocoon shops to use them. The loan is secured by the machines purchased by the cocoon shops and their income, and the Silk Control Association provides a second guarantee. The cocoon shops in Zhejiang Province have now registered with the association to purchase the machines. It is expected that they will be purchased and distributed to various cocoon shops when the spring cocoons are put on the market next year.

Incentives to Increase Seed Production

The association has also recognized that there has been a shortage of domestic silkworm seeds in recent years. If measures are not taken to increase seed production as soon as possible, not only will there be more panic in the future, but ordering from abroad when there is a shortage of silkworm seeds will result in more losses and outflow of profits. This must be remedied urgently. It is now negotiating with the Agricultural and Commercial Bureau of the Ministry of Industry to borrow 200,000 yuan to provide to various seed breeding farms for expansion of equipment, so that production can be increased in the future to meet the needs of rural areas in various regions. The Agricultural and Commercial Bureau has agreed in principle to the loan and has sent personnel to Hangzhou for investigation. It is expected that a formal contract will be signed soon, and the matter will be handled.

Various Old Stamps to be Discontinued on a Specific Date 118

Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1373 states that, according to the order of the Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications: "It has been found that old-version ordinary stamps, airmail stamps, postage due stamps, and postcard postal stationery have been approved by the Executive Yuan through the Ministry of Communications to be sold only until December 31, 1936. After the cessation of sales, they can still be used as usual for one month (i.e., from January 1, 1937, to January 31, 1937). From February 1, 1937, they will be officially discontinued and will no longer be used. However, if the public has any unused stamps at that time, they will be allowed to exchange them for new-version ordinary stamps of the same value (i.e., stamps with the portraits of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and revolutionary martyrs) at various post offices within six months after the discontinuation (i.e., from February 1, 1937, to July 31, 1937). After the deadline, no exchange will be allowed." According to this order, the list of old-version stamps, postcards, and postal stationery is listed below for public information. This notice lists: sailboat style, agricultural harvest style, garden gate style, ordinary stamps, blue and brown postage due stamps, sailboat style single and double postcards, Jiahe style Chinese and foreign text three-cent postal stationery, and two-color airmail stamps issued in 1929. Director Zha Peilin, December 4.

Sun Hengfu Sued for Damaging Creditor Rights by Riding in His Son's Car: Nai Zi Owes Baoshen Bank Debts and Transferred the Car to His Father, Resulting in the Lawsuit 121

Sun Xianggui, the former director of the Ningbo Siming Bank, is the son of Sun Hengfu, the former general manager of Siming Bank. In 1931, when Sun was in office, he had dealings with the Yongdi Baoshen Bank. As a result, he owed the bank 27,500 yuan. Because Sun delayed repayment, He Lianguan, the manager of the bank, hired lawyer Xu Jie in Shanghai to file a lawsuit for delay, which has been decided, and Sun has lost the case. He then filed a lawsuit for enforcement. During the enforcement process, Sun repeatedly failed to appear, and the enforcement court issued a warrant for his arrest, but he was not apprehended. Baoshen Bank also published advertisements in various newspapers seeking Sun's whereabouts, offering 500 yuan as a reward, but to no avail. He Lianguan has now learned that Sun Xianggui had a car with license plate number 98, which was suddenly transferred to his father, Sun Hengfu, to ride in. This is a violation of Article 355 of the Criminal Law, damaging creditor rights. Therefore, He hired lawyer Xu to file a criminal lawsuit in the First Special Court, requesting that he be punished as deserved. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Pan Zhenyang opened the Fifth Criminal Court for interrogation. Sun Xianggui did not appear. His wife hired lawyer Yuan Hanyun to appear in court, stating that Sun had gone blind after his business failed and had gone to Japan for treatment. According to his telegram, he cannot appear in court. He Lianguan then submitted a statement of the case, stating that although the loan was only over 27,000 yuan, it would amount to over 40,000 yuan including interest. Although the defendant has status, it is difficult to ascertain his assets. Even a car has been transferred to his father. And the subpoena from your court to Sun Hengfu was entrusted to the defendant for delivery, but the defendant's family claimed not to know this person. How can a son not know his father? Lawyer Yuan completely acknowledged the loan between the defendant and the plaintiff but stated that the defendant's car was a Dodge and was mortgaged to Hengxun Bank last year. This car is now being ridden by Yu Zuoting, and the license plate has been changed to number 4614, while Sun Hengfu's car license plate was originally number 4271. Because his son's car was sold, he took the 98 license plate back for his own use. Therefore, there was no damage to creditor rights. Plaintiff's lawyer Xu Jie believed that Yuan's claim was inconsistent and submitted a reply from the Vehicle Management Office to the court. Judge Pan checked the report and ordered a postponement for investigation and further interrogation. He also notified lawyer Yuan to order the defendant to appear in court.

Private Red Pill Manufacturing Operation Cracked Down 122

On the morning of the day before yesterday, Chinese and Western detectives from the French Concession learned that someone was secretly manufacturing the poisonous Qin Xing brand red pills at 171 Thistledew Lane for sale in the city. At 11 o'clock at noon, they went to the address to search and arrested the manufacturers, Min native Yang Mingxuan (25 years old), Yang Alai (28 years old), and Nanjing native Zhou Jinrong (24 years old), among others. They confiscated 117 red pills, over ten pounds of raw materials, and a complete set of handmade red pill equipment and brought them back to the police station. Lawyer Gu Shouxi of the Police Department explained the case and requested a postponement for investigation before requesting a trial. The court checked the report, questioned the defendants separately, and ordered a postponement for 15 days for further interrogation. The defendants were returned to custody.

Li Guocheng, the Murder Case Defendant, Awaits Judgment After Retrial 123

On the afternoon of August 13, 1931, at 6 p.m., a case of Jiangbei bandits killing their own kind occurred in the Fasheng Inn on Xixinqiao Street in the French Concession. Jiang Zhonghan, Xia Yongsheng, and a man surnamed Xue were killed, and Zhong Ziqing was injured. Later, the French police arrested a suspect named Yan Jinbiao. He was sentenced to death by the Second Special Court, and the verdict was final. The original sentence was carried out according to law. During the interrogation, Yan confessed that the mastermind was Li Guocheng from Funing, also known as Chen Youliang. In January 1933, Li was handed over to the Public Security Bureau by Yan's family in Rihui Port. After the Second Special Court brought him back for trial, he was also sentenced to death and deprived of his civil rights for life. Li refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Third High Court, but the appeal was rejected. Li then appealed to the Supreme Court, which sent the case back for retrial. On July 6 of the previous year, the Third High Court changed the sentence to life imprisonment. Li still refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Supreme Court again. Now, the Supreme Court has reviewed the case and determined that there has been a general amnesty, but the original trial did not mention it. Therefore, it has revoked the original sentence and sent it back to the Third High Court for another retrial. Yesterday afternoon, presiding judge Wu Tingqi, along with judges Liao and Wang, and prosecutor Dong, presided over the retrial in the Third Criminal Court. Lawyer Fei Xizhen appeared in court on behalf of the French Police Department. After the court questioned the appellant Li Guocheng about the case and the reasons for the appeal, it ordered the opening of the debate. The debate was concluded, and the verdict was scheduled to be announced at 2 p.m. on the 12th. The appellant was returned to custody.

Zhoujiazui Road: Chinese Police Struggle with Robbers Last Night, Resulting in One Robber Killed on the Spot, One Captured Alive, and the Rest Escaping 125

At the Xie Tai Grain Store at No. 157 Zhoujiazui Road, four robbers suddenly arrived at around 8 p.m. last night. Two robbers were wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants, and the other two were wearing overcoats. They broke into the store, two robbers guarded the back door, and the other robbers took out pistols, scaring everyone into silence. They robbed more than 70 yuan in legal tender from the counter and fled out the door. The store staff, after the robbers had left, immediately shouted "Robbery!" and frantically blew the police whistle. Two Chinese police officers from Nos. 1231 and 377 nearby heard the sound and rushed over, seeing four robbers running away in front. The two police officers immediately chased after them. The robbers opened fire to resist arrest, and the police officers also returned fire. The chase reached the intersection of Rue Auca, and three more police officers, Nos. 3055, 53, and 1913, joined in the pursuit. They worked together to subdue one of the robbers wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants. He was shot several times and died on the spot. The remaining robbers continued to open fire to resist arrest and fled east. The police officers bravely stepped forward and captured one robber, while the other two robbers escaped without a trace. At the time, a passerby named Zhou Keming from Rugao, who was pulling a rickshaw, was hit in the right leg by a stray bullet and was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by a police car. The captured robber was taken to the police station in charge for investigation. The body of the killed robber was sent to the coroner's office for examination.

After discussion, it was decided to publish the information in the Ningbo and Fenghua newspapers to solicit recognition, and to inquire among fellow villagers to see if there were any other county locations. After verifying the facts, the matter will be handled accordingly, and a letter will be sent to reply to the association. The meeting adjourned at 7 p.m.

Chemical Raw Materials Industry Association Held Third Reorganization Committee Meeting Yesterday 129

The Shanghai Chemical Raw Materials Industry Association has been legally organized and established for several years. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Party Department ordered Fang Yexian, chairman of Zhaoxin Chemical Factory, Cai Shichong, manager of China Alcohol Factory, Shen Zhongyi, chairman of Jiangnan Chemical Manufacturing Factory, Zhu Wenqi, chairman of Dazhong Raw Material Factory, Lu Zhixue, general manager of Kaicheng Acid Factory, Xie Xiaochu, manager of Jiangnan Chemical Factory, and Lin Dian, manager of Dafeng Industrial Raw Material Factory, and Xie Zhongfu, general manager of Dacheng Glue Factory, to be reorganization members. It was proposed that this matter be discussed. The meeting decided that (1) members should be notified again to make every effort to donate to support the defense of Suiyuan; (2) a letter should be submitted to the Party Department for approval regarding similar organizations organized without the permission of Party and government agencies in order to maintain law and order; (3) a corrected announcement should be published in the newspaper immediately to correct public opinion. The meeting then adjourned.

Former Literary Scholar Sun Shizheng Lays Out Funeral Arrangements 133

Mr. Sun Shizheng is a descendant of Yuan Xiang. His home is in Dabudao Lane, Changshu, which is the former site of Tianzhen Pavilion. Mr. Shizheng worked as an official in Peiping, so he always lived in the old capital, almost considering it his second hometown. He served as secretary-general of the Ministry of Finance and Communications, and supervisor of the Capital University, etc. His name is known overseas, and he has friends from all over the world. Many of the key figures in the current central government are his close friends. He has published more than 20 French collections. The book "Reading the Classics to Save the Country" is his masterpiece. Last year, he reached the age of seventy and died of dampness in Peiping. At that time, his family and his disciples Qi Liuzhe and Tang Zongguo, etc. organized a funeral office in Peiping to handle funeral affairs. This spring, his nephew Lun Chai went to Peiping to collect the coffin, and his son Binghuang and his disciples escorted it to his hometown of Changshu, temporarily placing the coffin in Xiaoyunqi Temple in preparation for choosing a date for burial. It is now learned that his family and old friends in his hometown have organized a funeral office in his old residence, and have chosen January 3 of the national calendar to lay out funeral arrangements for him in Jufengyuan in Changshu City. The next day will be the burial. It is expected that at that time, the plain cars and white horses, and those who come to pay their respects from afar, will definitely be very crowded.

Shen Bao National Products Special Issue

A New Development in the Future of National Products 137

— Xuan Wan

—Planning to Establish a National Products Joint Venture Company

In the midst of the arduous and enthusiastic promotion of the national products movement, there has recently been a new development in the future of our national products.

This new development is that the National Economic Construction Movement Committee in Nanjing recently brought together government banks and the China National Products Production and Sales Association to plan the establishment of a nationwide national products joint venture company with a capital of two million yuan. Recently, national products magnates from Shanghai went to Nanjing to discuss the matter with Director Wu. Subsequently, the association announced the formation of a preparatory committee of 39 people to actively carry out the preparations, laying the foundation for the national economic construction of our country and the initial revitalization of national industry. In the current situation, it also demonstrates the government's determination to maintain domestic products and the achievements of the national products sector over the years!

Originally, due to the rise of the national national products movement in recent years, the self-awareness of the general industrial sector has been promoted, and they have all engaged in the development of the national products industry. Not only has the number of national products factories increased, but also national products companies, national products stores, and national products malls have been established like a rising wind and surging clouds in various places. However, its only defect is that there is no national national products sales headquarters to systematically control, improve, and expand them. Therefore, the government and the national industrial sector have joined hands to establish this joint venture company in order to overcome the past phenomenon of being scattered and acting independently, so that the future of national products will have new developments and promote the national government's main task of managing national production and sales.

Although, at this time, we still hope that the national products sector will make its own efforts to improve its products and increase production quantities, and that the government will effectively reward those who promote the sales of national products, reduce transportation costs and taxes, so that national products will sell better. This is an important prerequisite in the process of implementing the national national products production and sales network.

In short, in the past, the center of our national products movement was often focused on empty words and verbal propaganda, but now we have further strived to practically establish a national planned and organized production and sales mechanism. This spirit of progressive overall planning reflects that the future of our national products has a new development. We must continue this spirit, encourage ourselves to progress, and create a greater and more glorious future for national products!

National Products Sector and the Industrial Association Law 138

— Yang An

Recently, the Ministry of Industry has drafted three types of association laws: the Commercial Association Law, the Industrial Association Law, and the Export Association Law. After five or six months of discussion and more than ten meetings, the draft was finally completed and submitted to the Executive Yuan for consultation and transmission to the Legislative Yuan for approval. The comprehensiveness and prudence of the formulation of our country's industrial and commercial association laws this time is the greatest. The pain that our national products sector has felt over the years is as follows:

(1) Unnecessary competition among the same industry, mutual killing.

(2) Each factory has its own way of collecting raw materials, manufacturing technology, and promotion methods, without contact with each other.

(3) The organization among the same industry often presents a scattered and complex state, even overlapping and creating extra branches, losing the function of control.

(4) Due to the lack of contact among the same industry on weekdays, there is a lack of research on business, guidance on technology, and all statistical surveys are lacking. The prosperity and decline of the same industry is not easy to understand.

This draft of the Industrial Association Law is aimed at these drawbacks. It strives for the improvement and development of industry, corrects past shortcomings, and takes cooperation as its main purpose. Common purchase of raw materials and cooperative management of warehouses and transportation are all essential elements for the future development of the industrial sector. It is hoped that the national products sector will earnestly study the draft formulated by the Ministry of Industry, and make statements as far as experience allows, for the government's reference. Legislation is one thing, and facts are another. Whether legal principles and facts can adapt and whether they can be implemented without creating difficulties all require empirical consideration. Our industrial sector is most closely related to this and should pay attention to it urgently.

— Zhen Ru

Please refer to issue 193 of this publication. I am pleased to learn that the Shanghai Women's National Products Consumption Association was officially established on November 11th. Okay, whether you are a member or not, everyone remember November 11th, everyone don't forget local products and soil goods, then national products will naturally develop, and the leak can be plugged, so that we will not fail the auspicious day and time of the establishment of this association.

Clean and Inexpensive National Product Stoves 141

— Yin Sheng

The north wind has risen and the cold has struck. Stoves are truly a blessing in the home, and are essential for those above the middle class. What kind of stove is the best and most suitable for our ideal conditions on the market now? This is also a common sense that should be possessed when winter comes.

Recently, clean and inexpensive stoves have appeared on the market, which can eliminate the drawbacks of old stoves and revolutionize the fate of old stoves. There are several ways in which they are completely different from old-style stoves:

(1) The stove door has only one - because there is no need to add coal or hook out ashes, there is no need for multiple doors, only one air door is enough. After the fire is lit, this air door is also tightly closed, so there is no smoke or ash all day long, and the room is naturally clean. (Old-style doors have three or four, and must be opened from time to time, with smoke and ash filling the air, which is extremely annoying)

(2) The flue is smaller - the coal burned in ordinary stoves does not provide enough air, and most of it turns into smoke and carbon, which is scattered in the air, making the air turbid, and accumulating in the pipe, causing the flue to become clogged. Therefore, the flue must be large. The coal used in clean stoves is specially made and burns completely, so there is very little soot. The flue does not need to be too large, and the heat is not leaked outwards, which can save coal and expenses.

(3) Specially made coal crystals - the advantages of coal crystals are (A) only one is used per day, and the remaining ash does not break after burning, but remains in one piece and can be easily removed, (B) clean, with no ash or smoke, as mentioned above, (C) there are three sizes of coal crystals. If you want to increase the heat, you can use the large size. If you want to save money, you can use the medium and small sizes, which are very flexible, (D) they do not take up much space. The coal crystals are the same size and can be stacked in the corner of the wall, only two or three feet is enough, unlike loose coal, which requires a large amount, takes up a lot of space, and is messy all over the ground.

(4) Can be used for two purposes - institutions or large families who burn coal stoves in the kitchen all day and all year round to get boiling water or cook dishes can use this stove instead, with no added cost and more convenience.

(5) Even heat - ordinary stoves, when adding coal, the heat drops sharply, and when the fire is lit, the heat is too high. Uneven cold and heat often leads to sore throats or colds, and children are prone to getting sick. Clean stoves use coal crystals, so the heat is uniform all day long, and there is no sudden rise or fall in heat, which is beneficial to health and is very important.

Other things such as the elegance of the stove style and the low price are secondary matters. It is heard that this stove was designed by a professor at Central University, referring to the latest foreign-style stoves, and after several improvements, it was finally launched on the market and will soon be available.

Educational News

Japanese Universities Implement National Defense Education: Tokyo, Osaka, and Kyushu Imperial Universities Establish Aeronautics Departments, Military and Aeronautical Science Expenses Increase by Hundreds of Thousands 143

(Special Dispatch from Tokyo) The Japanese Ministry of Education, in order to implement national defense education, has made new regulations regarding the special budget for directly controlled schools in the coming year. The funding for aeronautical science, military industrial lectures, and special national defense research institutes has been reviewed and approved by the Ministry of Finance, as described below: (1) Regarding aviation, the most urgent task is to cultivate specialized technical personnel for manufacturing aircraft. Therefore, in the budget for the coming year, 150,000 yen will be used to expand the aeronautics department of Tokyo Imperial University, increasing the current four lectureships to six, and the student quota from ten to twenty-five. Furthermore, 400,000 yen will be used to establish new aeronautics departments at Osaka and Kyushu Imperial Universities, with a student quota of ten each. Additionally, 450,000 yen will be used to establish aeronautical engineering departments at Yokohama and Nagoya Higher Technical Schools, with a student quota of twenty each. (2) National defense education research institutions are also being established one after another. 500,000 yen will be used at the joint research laboratory and factory of the engineering department of Tokyo Imperial University to establish a comprehensive testing institute, including all departments of the engineering faculty, for trial production purposes. 680,000 yen will be used at the Tokyo Institute of Technology to establish a precision machinery research institute. 20,000 yen each will be used to establish lectureships in chemical machinery at Tohoku Imperial University, lectureships in liquid fuel at Hokkaido Imperial University, and lectureships in pharmacology at Osaka Imperial University. 200,000 yen will be used to subsidize the coal liquefaction and artificial wool research at the Koushang Research Institute of Kyoto Imperial University. The newly added national defense education budget mentioned above has been fully approved by the Ministry of Finance and will be implemented starting next year. It is reported that all universities will begin preparations on December 1st. (Qin Er—Nine)

Restrictions on Graduation Qualifications for Schools Above the Specialized Level Stipulated by the Ministry of Education 147

Order No. 18125 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to the Ministry of Education: "Upon investigation, if the graduation certificate of a graduate from a public or formerly registered private specialized school or school above the specialized level is lost, and the original school has been closed, and they apply to the Ministry for certification of their professional qualifications, the Ministry has granted approval and certification upon verification of the case. However, the number of such applications has been increasing, and if no measures are taken to restrict them, irregularities may occur. For the sake of prudence, three articles of restrictions on the application for certification of graduation qualifications after the loss of a graduation certificate are formulated to be followed by those who have the necessity for such an application. As for cases where the original school is still in existence, the restrictions on this application should be handled in accordance with Articles 1 and 2 of the aforementioned measures. A copy of the measures is enclosed for your department to be informed." The Department, upon receiving the order, yesterday notified the specialized schools and schools above the specialized level under its jurisdiction. The restrictions on applying for certification of graduation qualifications after the loss of a professional certificate are recorded below: 1. If a graduation certificate of a graduate from a public or formerly registered private specialized school or school above the specialized level is lost, and the original school has been closed, and they apply to the Ministry for certification of their graduation qualifications, the following regulations apply: (1) The reason for the loss of the graduation certificate must be published in a prominent local newspaper for more than three days, declaring the aforementioned loss invalid (newspaper attached). (2) A list including the applicant's name, gender, age, place of origin, name of the original graduating school, name of the original school principal, department or group, date of admission and graduation, etc., must be provided, along with two two-and-a-half-inch half-length photos of the applicant. (3) A certificate of truthful proof from two or more former faculty members of the original school or currently serving appointed-rank civil servants (signed and sealed, the certifier shall bear corresponding responsibility if the testimony does not match the facts). 2. If the original school is still in existence and the applicant applies to the original school for investigation and certification of graduation qualifications, the regulations in the aforementioned (1) and (2) apply.

General Situation of Shanghai Municipal Council Elementary Schools (6) 157

— Special Report by This Newspaper, Investigation by Hu Zuyin

Starting in 1935, the school medical office specially set up three free trachoma treatment centers, with ten consultation sessions per week. Students in each school can take turns to receive treatment twice a week. During the winter and summer vacations, the number of consultations for trachoma treatment is increased to allow more students with trachoma to receive treatment. In total, last year, 1,598 students in the five Chinese children's elementary schools suffered from mild to severe trachoma. The total number of consultations throughout the year was 24,146. 272 students were completely cured. The condition of 179 students gradually improved, which is satisfactory. 250 students who had recovered were re-examined. 72 students relapsed after being cured. The reason for the relapse is due to the lack of emphasis on public health in the family.

For students who have contracted infectious diseases, serious illnesses, or other minor illnesses, in addition to notifying their parents to seek medical treatment, the school medical office also sends school nurses to visit the sick students' homes to find out whether the students' parents have sought medical treatment for their children. This kind of visiting work is quite valuable; on the one hand, it can clarify the situation of students receiving medical treatment at home, and on the other hand, it can persuade and urge parents to pay attention to and implement the work of maintaining children's health. The following table shows the records of school nurses visiting students' families, which also shows the value of this work.

First visit to students' families 2,523 people

Students' parents have carried out various medical treatments 1,075 people

Students' parents have not taken any action 1,448 people

Second visit to students' families 2,395 people

Students' parents have carried out various medical treatments 1,425 people

Students' parents have not taken any action 970 people

Third visit to students' families 1,957 people

Students' parents have carried out various medical treatments 1,268 people

Students' parents have not taken any action 689 people

Special visit to students' families during the holidays 458 people

Students' parents have carried out various medical treatments 401 people

Students' parents have not taken any action 57 people

Looking at the above table, it can be seen that the tendency of parents not taking action for children's diseases has gradually decreased; this can also prove that, as a result of school nurses visiting students' families, students' parents have paid attention to the health of children in school.

Thirteen. Family Liaison

The Shanghai Municipal Council elementary schools usually welcome parents to come to the school for talks. During each semester, each school holds a grade-level reception for parents to have talks, and teachers from each school take turns to receive parents of each grade to come to the school for talks. In this kind of talk, teachers and parents can exchange views on the personality, physical and psychological condition of the children, as well as various opinions on raising children. Teachers can also take this opportunity to give parents the children's usual homework results and ten-week test results for viewing, so that parents can understand the children's academic situation in school. According to the school authorities, this kind of grade-level reception for parents to have talks is of great help to the communication and liaison between school and family.

Commercial News

Grain and Flour See Strong Buying Interest - Opening Prices for Each Month Nearly Rise to the One Corner Limit - Although Retreating Midway, Prices Ultimately Remain Firm and High 169

Yesterday's flour market saw unabated frenzy from the opening bell. Prices for all months rose almost to the one corner limit, threatening another standstill. The bullish performance gave the impression of disregard for all else. When the opening prices were quoted, foreign wheat prices had already risen by two or three jiao, so the price for the current month jumped by six or seven fen. As a result, the price for January rose by one jiao, and trading came to a standstill. Unexpectedly, there was a reaction after the second session, as both bulls took profits and factories dumped large quantities, causing the market to gradually loosen. Except for the current month, prices for all months fell by six, seven, or eight fen, showing significant fluctuations. At the opening of the afternoon session, fluctuations for the current month were not significant, but news spread that Tianjin's spot flour prices were good, reviving buying interest. Once trading resumed, prices rebounded by three or five fen compared to the morning close. Given the unstable environment, it is feared that the turbulence will not subside easily.

The Wheat Futures Market Sees a Dangerous Situation at High Prices - Trading Halted in the Morning Due to Unpaid Margin Calls - Afternoon Trading Sees Minor Fluctuations - Spot Wheat Prices Rise Again by More Than One Corner 170

The wheat futures market halted trading yesterday morning because margin calls had not been fully paid. Trading resumed as usual in the afternoon. As the opening prices were announced, the erratic nature of the flour market led to active trading but smaller fluctuations. Although there was no reason for prices to fall in the current market turmoil, people inevitably became wary due to the high prices. As a result, the final prices for each month rose by only one, two, three, or four fen. Spot wheat prices rose by more than one corner across the board. Kai Gao You Wheat was quoted at 6 yuan 6 jiao, settling at 5 jiao 3 fen; Guan Dian Wheat at 6 yuan 6 jiao 8 fen, settling at 4 jiao 4 fen; Dao Ren Qiao Wheat at 6 yuan 5 jiao 3 fen, settling at 4 jiao 5 fen; Shaoxing Wheat at 6 yuan 9 jiao; Huaian Wheat at 6 yuan 5 jiao; and Anqing Wheat at 6 yuan 5 jiao, settling at 4 jiao 5 fen. Fufeng sold 8,000 bags.

Jiading County Detains Over 200 Rice Boats - Shanghai North Relies Solely on Nanpu Rice Boats for Supplies 171

(Shanghai North) Although eleven or twelve boats arrived from Nanpu yesterday, over 200 boats were detained in the Jiwangmiao area of Jiading County and have not been released, causing unease. As a result, rice prices have risen by one, two, three, or four jiao. Yesterday afternoon, leaders of the rice industry association took official documents to the Zhenjiang Provincial Government to request that Jiading County release the boats, which calmed the public and stabilized market prices slightly. Yesterday, the price of white japonica rice rose by one or two jiao, while Bianyuan rice soared by three or four jiao. Yangdujian rice rose by two jiao, while Baodao rice tightened by one jiao, and Kejian rice also tightened by one jiao. The prices of all other types of rice also increased.

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the supply from various origins was slightly scarce, with a total of over seventy boats arriving, carrying 14,300 to 14,400 dan of cargo. Baodao rice accounted for nearly fifty boats, and buying interest continued, though not as brisk as in the previous market. However, the market was still good, with a total of over 6,000 bags of Baodao rice from Pingjin, Qingyan, and other origins being sold, and prices rising by two jiao. Over 4,000 bags of thick japonica rice were sold, with prices rising by about two jiao. However, considering the overall trend, the large volume of sales recently can be attributed to the baozi (steamed bun) market, so changes in the thick and thin japonica rice markets depend on this shift. Duyangjian also increased by one or two jiao, and Yinyuan also showed improvement, increasing by different amounts.

Imported Rice Prices Remain Firm 172

--Customer Xian Rice Sales are Particularly Brisk… The Market Rises Again by More Than One Corner—

Yesterday, customer xian rice digestion remained strong. In addition to continuous sales from both northern and southern customer merchants, local merchants and stockpilers also gradually became active. Due to the detention of river rice and the overall soaring of grain prices, the local spot sales and stockpilers' spirits were boosted. Customer merchants were still actively selling northern rice from Henan and other places, as well as Shantou rice, and newly added Quanzhou rice was also actively sold. Guangdong merchants had no intention of continuous active sales due to the supply of Hunan rice and the tax exemption on imported rice. Although there were transactions yesterday, they were only token. However, after continuous sales from customer stockpilers and local merchants, with a daily volume of 16,000 bags, people's confidence has been boosted. Yesterday, the market continued to rise by one jiao to one jiao five or six fen. The total daily sales included 545 bags of Jiangxi rice, 2,911 bags of Hunan rice, 500 bags of Han brown rice, 2,150 bags of Wentaiyong rice, 300 bags of Jiangbei rice. Imported rice prices remained high. Yesterday, foreign merchants reported that Saigon rice was priced at 14.5 yuan per tael in Shanghai, and broken rice, after full taxation, would also cost 13 yuan three or four jiao.

With No Incoming Soybean Supply, Soybean Prices Become Increasingly Excited - The Result of Not Seeking Self-Sufficiency in Food 173

The soybean market advanced amid the volatile rise in Dalian. Currently, the supply from the Northeast is inevitably reduced, and wheel soybeans are not abundant. Therefore, people are very excited. Yarn and Cotton - This Month's Yarn Futures Return to Ten Yuan Below the Highest Price - Rumors of Qingdao Labor Unrest Being Resolved - Many Long Positions Have Been Mostly Liquidated 174

After the sharp rise in the yarn market, a sudden reversal occurred, with a dramatic decline. In fact, the daily rapid rise was too large, making this kind of sharp decline unsurprising. This newspaper anticipated that it would fall ten yuan below the peak, and this month's futures have now fallen ten yuan. However, the spot yarn market is dull, as the end of the year is approaching, and business may experience a period of quiet. However, major players have not given up on absorbing inventory.

Prices for Futures in Each Month Fall

The pre-market opening for standard yarn saw tight conditions for December, rising by six jiao. Upon trading in the January futures, the market sentiment suddenly reversed, with a selling wave emerging. This was due to the Qingdao yarn factory's resumption of work issue, which was expected to be resolved satisfactorily, leading to a more bearish sentiment. At the second session opening, the December futures plummeted by three yuan and five jiao, and the distant months fell by another one yuan six or seven jiao. At the same time, spot yarn trading was sluggish, and the situation remained weak. As a result, each month fell by two yuan and five jiao to four yuan and four jiao compared to the previous day's close. At the afternoon opening, major players were still buying near-term contracts, while floating accounts continued to sell distant months, softening the market further. The market situation remained peaceful thereafter, with most long positions being liquidated and a large amount being sold. Market prices gradually declined. As a result, each month fell by another five jiao to one yuan two jiao compared to the morning close. 2,150 bales were sold by Dayi, 2,200 bales by Minde, 5,500 bales by Hexing, 1,250 bales by Gengfeng, 2,350 bales by Wang Taixing, 3,000 bales by Dachangcheng, 1,050 bales by Minghua, 500 bales by Yicheng, and 750 bales by Xiecheng. Indian Cotton Prices Gradually Converge - Cotton Merchants Sell on Rallies - In Light of the Sharp Rise in Flour and Wheat, Cotton Futures Also Want to Go Long 175

The cotton market is sluggish, but in light of the sharp rise in flour and wheat prices, people outside the industry also see cotton prices rising, resulting in a large amount of speculative buying. However, the overseas cotton market is unusually dull, so most traders adopt a "sell on rallies" strategy.

Cotton Prices Ease as Soon as They Rise

Pre-market opening for standard cotton saw continued high prices in the near months. Due to the surge in flour and wheat prices, gold and securities merchants absorbed inventory and did not release it. However, upon trading in the distant months, traders, noting the lackluster overseas Indian and American cotton markets and the converging prices of Indian cotton, tended to sell, causing prices to fall. The second session saw a sharp drop of three, four, or five jiao. The third closing was uneventful. As a result, each month fell by one jiao to three jiao and a half compared to the previous day's close. At the afternoon opening, prices were nearly firm in the distant months. Most merchants who bought yarn and sold cotton had already hedged their positions, tightening the market slightly. The second and third sessions saw slight upward movement. By the close, traders were selling, causing distant months to fall back by two jiao and a half. As a result, each month rose or fell by five fen to one jiao compared to the morning close. Yongchang sold 1,500 dan, Yuda sold 2,300 dan, Gengyun sold 3,800 dan, Renfeng sold 4,300 dan, Xingchang sold 1,800 dan, Dachangcheng sold 3,800 dan, Yuanxingchang sold 4,800 dan, Yikang sold 2,100 dan, Dafeng sold 3,800 dan, Hexing sold 2,800 dan, Taixing sold 2,300 dan, and Taichang sold 1,300 dan. The American Cotton Market is Largely Firm - But Seems to Lack New Stimulation 177

The American cotton market opened yesterday with sluggish conditions. Traders are waiting for the government report to be released. The political situation in the UK prompted cotton farmers to hedge and foreign long positions to liquidate. However, the selling pressure was not strong, and all selling was absorbed by traders, resulting in mixed prices. Each month fell by two pounds to rise by two pounds. Judging from the market trend, it is largely firm, but lacking new stimulation. According to traders' predictions, there will be no major changes in the government report's harvest quantity. When the market closed, traders bought, and the market became firmer again. Spot prices rose by four points, and the near-term contract fell by three points to rise by five points. Spot English cotton fell by three points, and futures fell by one point. Individual buying of Indian cotton was overturned by cotton merchants' hedging. Pynguel fell by 0.25 rupees, Omra fell by 0.5 to 0.75 rupees, and Balaras fell by 0.75 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (7th dispatch).

According to a Bombay dispatch, the opening forecast for the 8th was: Balaras at 219 rupees, Omra at 198 rupees, and Pynguel at 160.5 rupees, all up by 0.25 rupees.

A New York telegram on the 7th stated that the US Cotton Fifth Government Report is scheduled to be released at noon on the 8th. Based on various private estimates, the predicted production is 12,265,000 bales, and the amount ginned is 11,417,000 bales.

All Rangoon Cotton Exports Last Week Went to Shanghai 179

A Bombay dispatch on the 7th stated that the total amount of cotton exported from Rangoon last week was 26 tons, all of which went to Shanghai.

Three Commodities, Yarn, and Cotton All Rise 180

An Osaka telegram on the 8th stated that the prices of three commodities' futures rose by two yuan to three yuan and nine jiao. The near month was 245 yuan, and the distant month was 222 yuan and four jiao. Cotton futures rose by three jiao to six jiao and five fen. The near month was 67 yuan and five jiao, and the distant month was 68 yuan and four jiao and five fen.

Piece Goods: Although Both Futures and Spot Yarn and Thread Have Fallen, the Cotton Cloth Market Remains Firm Due to Shortages 181

Yesterday's cloth market saw slackened sentiment due to the report that the Qingdao factory's resumption of work issue would be resolved satisfactorily, and the counter-movement decline of standard yarn, regulated yarn, and thread. Fine cloth and fine twill's spot sales have already waned. Coarse cloth, coarse twill, velvet, zhigong, serge, and flannel prices remain firm because each factory's inventory is exhausted and incoming goods from inland factories are scarce. The selling market is gradually stabilizing, and it is still difficult to obtain goods. Tianjin merchants in the north road continue to show strong interest in buying, with transactions for over 500 pieces of goods, including white velvet, flannel, zhigong, serge, standard cloth, printed satin, zhigong, and serge. Goods to be delivered to the inland area in succession account for half of the transactions. Merchants from Henan, Sichuan, and the Yangtze River areas also made many transactions. Local and inland merchants are most actively trading colored cloth, velvet, heavy and light coarse cloth. Merchants from Fujian, who had been inactive for a long time, have gradually started buying again, while merchants from Guangdong and Yunnan have slackened their demand for all goods.

Finance: Standard Gold Becomes the "Standard Standard" - The Listed Opening and Closing Prices are Both 1155 Yuan and Four Jiao 182

Yesterday's gold market saw a sudden decline in buying interest. Although pure gold rose, the opening was relatively stable, but it was only a fleeting phenomenon. Major players mostly liquidated their positions and gradually became bearish. Overseas silver markets, both British and American, were flat, and the forward silver price in Monte Rea contracted by one and a half to four points. Exchange rates rose slightly, and London spot gold rose by one and a half pence. The central bank's listed price announcement showed that both British and American prices were flat, the customs gold unit rose by two points, and the standard gold price was listed at 1155 yuan and four jiao. The off-market pre-trading opened, rising to 56 yuan due to slight buying by Jingfu and others. The morning opening was high, but major players continued to sell and became bearish. The mid-day trading fluctuated very little. HSBC's listed price announcement showed that both British and American prices were flat, and the silver balance tax announcement remained unchanged, gradually declining. Spot merchants took advantage of the low price to make small purchases and support the market. Later, the supply was limited, and the market fluctuated greatly at noon. The after-market was very quiet. Although spot merchants bought, it had little impact. As a result, it remained consistent with the standard price. The market conditions for the day are recorded below:

The morning opening was 1156 yuan, up three jiao from the previous closing. Yuen Feng, Yongde, and Xianghe sold off, reaching 5 yuan and four jiao. Hengyun, Yongjin, and Fengyong bought slightly, rising to 5 yuan and six jiao. Yuan Feng, Yongxing, Yongdade, and Chenglian sold in unison. HSBC's listed price announcement retreated to five yuan and two jiao. Tongfeng Silver Balance Tax remained unchanged, gradually moving downstream and retreating to five yuan and two jiao. Chen Yong, Shen Da Yong, Hong Chang Yong, and Qian Chang Xiang bought slightly, and Xianghe also bought, rising to five yuan and a half. Hengyu Tongyu Run sold off, retreating to five yuan and three jiao. Yuan Feng Yong bought again, and the noon closing was 1155 yuan and four jiao.

The after-market opening was 1155 yuan and a half. Although Tongfeng Heng bought, Yuan Feng and Yongyou had selling interest, and Hengyu also sold, retreating to five yuan and four jiao. The Indian silver exchange was fixed at a total of two ana, and the closing remained at 1155 yuan and four jiao.

The closing price was 1155 yuan and four jiao, following the central bank's standard gold price listing. The market was essentially flat, with the January ledger price at 1155 yuan and the morning replenishment at 1153 yuan. The spot market remained firm, with Tianjin goods quoted at an additional 13 yuan and a half, and Qichi's buying price at 11 yuan. There were no transactions. The selling price was quoted at an additional 15 yuan. Tongfeng Heng sold 70 taels to Laofengxiang, and Shengyuan Yong sold 70 taels to Qingtianbao.

Trading in the market was limited. In summary, Yuanfeng Yong, Yongde, Xianghe, Qianchangxiang, Jingfu, Tongfeng Hengfu Da, and others were on the buying side, while Hengyu Yuanmao Yong, Yuanfeng Yong, Dade Cheng, Fuxing Yong, and others were on the selling side.

The market turned bearish throughout the day. The morning opening was 1156 yuan, and the closing was 1155 yuan and four jiao. The highest price was 1156 yuan, and the lowest price was 1155 yuan, with a fluctuation of eight jiao. As a result, it retreated by three jiao compared to the previous closing. The January futures' chips were reduced to 5,005 pieces, with a total of 30 long positions and 26 short positions. The total number of transactions was 238 pieces in the morning market and 21 pieces in the after-market.

Securities - Government Bonds Suddenly Rise with a Strong Surge 184

Yesterday in the Chinese Commercial Securities Exchange, the government bond market was experiencing a robust uptrend. After a long period of consolidation, the situation eased slightly, and sentiment turned from fatigue to firmness. Major players were actively buying, and many retail investors followed suit. The market was bullish due to strong buying interest, and the trading floor also looked promising. However, under stable environmental and market conditions, the bond market is not expected to undergo drastic changes. Yesterday morning, the trend was firm from the opening, and major players were actively buying. Large amounts were absorbed for the 50, 35, and 16 bonds, but the 10 and 5 bonds saw selling. Prices rose uniformly by two jiao and a half to six jiao. The closing was lively, and the market continued to advance. Major players such as the 35 and 32 bonds remained strong buyers, while the 10 and 43 bonds saw selling. Except for the Class A bonds expiring next month, which fell slightly by one jiao, all other bonds continued to rise by one or two jiao. The afternoon opening saw a mixed market. Many retail investors switched to cash, and the 5 bond also saw rolling over. Bonds such as the Tong, Wu, and Bing bonds retreated by one or two jiao. However, later, the 58 and 34 bonds and others resumed absorbing inventory. The Class B bonds expiring next month and the Class A bonds rose again by five fen and one jiao, respectively. At the closing, the market on the trading floor continued to look promising. The 34, 11, and 10 bonds and others continued to purchase, while the 35 and 50 bonds released some inventory. Prices continued to be firm, rising by five fen to three jiao and a half. As a result, prices rose across the board by four or five jiao to nine jiao. Silk and Tea - Raw Silk Exports Pale in Comparison 185

Exports of 5,156 Bales in the Second Half of November

The statistics for Shanghai's raw silk exports in the first half of November have already been reported in the previous newspaper. The statistics for the second half of the month are recorded below. Raw silk exports in the second half of the month totaled 3,760 bales, and Qingsi silk totaled 1,396 bales, totaling 5,156 bales, an increase of 419 bales compared to the first half of the month. However, when comparing the total for this year to date with last year, there is a huge decrease of 14,954 bales. Considering this figure, there are still many hidden worries for the future of the silk industry.

Statistics for Raw Silk Exports in the Second Half of November (unit: bale)

Some Transactions Made in Users Silk 186

Yesterday's overseas silk market was very soft. New York's near-term contracts fell by six points, and the distant-term contracts also fell by six points. The other Japanese silk 83 and 75 were sold evenly, falling by two to five points. Shanghai silk 78 and Guangdong silk both fell by one point. Dalian's silk market saw spot prices fall by 13 yuan, and futures prices fall by five yuan. It is expected that the market will be unstable and blunt. B-grade silk was sold at around 730 yuan. Local silk merchants were unwilling to sell. Indian merchants continued to make sporadic silk transactions. Only merchants from Hangzhou slightly increased their appetite for user silk, with prices falling by about five yuan.

Negotiations Underway for Large Transactions of Precious Tea 187

According to tea merchants, in the past two days, Ying Shang Jinlong Yangxing had a need to purchase common tea and eyebrow lu tea coming from Tunxi, Shexian and other places, so they invited the tea factories to discuss a purchase. They already have around 1,000 chests, and will soon close the deal in a few days. It is also heard that Yihe Xiehe and other foreign firms are also working towards separately numbering and sending cables to sell the remaining 5,000 chests of precious tea on the market. The situation is fermenting.

Miscellaneous News A Review of Wei Youfei's "China's Finance at the Present Stage" 188

— Liu Tang

In the past year, the changes in the financial industry have been drastic. Tracing the underlying motivations, some are external, and some are internal. Therefore, by following the causes and seeking the results, it becomes significantly complex. If there is no concrete treatise, not only will future generations find it complicated and difficult to understand, but even those in the current society will struggle to grasp the situation. Mr. Wei Youfei has, from November of the 24th year of the Republic to August of this year, collected extensive materials on the lead-up to and aftermath of the Chinese financial panic, as well as the significant developments in fiscal matters. This collection is indeed worthy of the title, "China's Finance at the Present Stage." Mr. Wei is one of the most attentive researchers of modern economics and a dedicated author. I believe that all the text is realistic, and the author himself hopes that it will be of some help to those studying China's economy and the economic changes of this period in the future. I share this sentiment and am happy to introduce it. Please inquire at the Ningbo Road Money Trade Monthly Office for general sales. The price is sixty cents.

Spring and Autumn

Sugar Market: Domestically Produced Green and Red Sugar Continue to Rise Sharply 189

Yesterday, due to a shortage of domestically produced green and red sugar arrivals, sellers vigorously raised prices. For example, new-batch green sugar opened at $34.80, an increase of $0.60-0.70, with over a hundred bags traded. Qilin (麒麟) and Laohu (老虎) brand fine red sugar opened at $16, with over two hundred bags traded, an increase of $0.50-0.60. Additionally, over a hundred bags of Shantong (善通) bag sugar were sold at $14.20, and over seventy ties of Qingyuan (慶元) slab green sugar at $11.60, an increase of $0.40.

The Public Association's benchmark prices remained relatively stable, with No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar spot goods at $21.55, regular re-export goods at $6.12, high-quality goods at $6.15, and No. 89 Shang (商) brand red sugar at $15.65, a slight increase. The original prices were maintained for cotton white sugar from local factories such as Zhenji (振記), Dahua (大華), and Jinxin (金心). Prices for Dong (東) brand white sugar Nos. 4, 8, and 9 also remained unchanged.

North and South Goods: Xiamen Tangerine Peel New Goods Arriving Soon 190

Old stock of Xiamen tangerine peel has long been out of stock. Yesterday, a letter from the production area stated that the new goods already show a bright red color and large size, and will be shipped to Shanghai soon. The cost is expected to be one or two dollars higher than the old stock. Upon arrival in Shanghai, due to empty warehouses, it should sell well.

Metals: Union Company Iron Price Rises Wildly 191

Price Fixed at $8.40 Gold Yuan; Scattered Transactions Extremely Busy

Since foreign countries in or near Zhenjiang [鎮江] have no [會] iron goods, the price is surprisingly firm, at $8.40 gold yuan per box, an increase of $0.40 from before (equivalent to about $36 in Shanghai market prices, including foreign taxes). Shanghai market counterparts, upon receiving this news, felt greatly encouraged, and dramatically increased their selling prices accordingly, now quoting $37. Although large-volume transactions are not numerous, scattered sales are exceptionally busy. It is estimated that the market released a total of four to five hundred boxes yesterday. Furthermore,囤戶 hoarders have recently been commissioning brokers to buy up supplies everywhere, so the market atmosphere is particularly good, and prices are feared to continue rising.

New Lead Wire Price Surprisingly High 192

Overseas prices for new lead wire have been steadily increasing recently. Yesterday, sizes 8, 10, 12, 14, and 16 were sold at £9 12s 6d per ton, another increase of 12s 6d from before. Sizes 16 to 20 required £10 5s per ton, also up 7s from before. It is said that the overseas market is surprisingly strong, and there is currently no spot stock. If counterparts place orders, they must wait until March for shipment. Shanghai market prices have also risen sharply in response to the brisk overseas prices, with selling prices increasing by $0.50 to $1.00 across the board.

Snippets 193

— Mingxin

Iron Chancellor Bismarck, upon ascending to the premiership, exerted his power to the fullest, promoting his unique ideas until Germany was revitalized. At that time, he once said to the representatives of the people: "The current problems can only be solved with iron and blood." We, the 470 million lonely and helpless people, crushed under the immeasurable national crisis, should also unanimously make the greatest determination and say to our own souls: "The current problems can only be solved with iron and blood."

If this can be genuinely expressed, it is foreseeable that in ten years, our old and great China will also rejuvenate, and like Germany rebuilt by Bismarck, will gradually become stronger and become a truly first-class power in the world. Then the sleeping lion will awaken, and the saying "dead pig" will truly be inaccurate. (Mingxin)

A Woman Who Doesn't Shed Tears 194

— Hualing

Who says women are good at crying? I don't believe it. Please let me present three recent events as proof. The first event concerns Mrs. Li, with whom I live. Mrs. Li has been married for seven years and is the mother of two children. Mr. Li treats her well, and the couple's relationship is quite harmonious. However, recently, Mrs. Li suddenly fell in love with her cousin, who is a section chief in a certain bank and recently widowed, and abruptly filed for divorce from Mr. Li. This was like a bolt from the blue for Mr. Li, who became so angry that he fell ill. In bed, he constantly shed tears, but Mrs. Li forced him to write a divorce letter and constantly threatened him. Unable to resist, Mr. Li gritted his teeth and succumbed with tears. Mrs. Li left that very night with the divorce letter. As she left, her three-year-old child was asleep, and her five-year-old child clung to her clothes, but she finally pushed the child away and left.

The second event is the death of my cousin. Before the coffin was even prepared, my cousin's wife concentrated on pressing her sixty-year-old in-laws for a dowry of ten thousand dollars. She eloquently told the relatives and friends present that her in-laws were unkind and usually cold. Now that her husband has died, the future is unimaginable, so she is making this request while relatives and friends are present to avoid future disputes. Her in-laws, grieving for the loss of their son and upset by her noise, burst into tears. But she showed no tears at all, instead speaking more energetically. Throughout my cousin's funeral, all we heard was her incessant chatter, without seeing her shed a single tear.

Another incident is the so-called "A-Geng's wife" in our neighborhood. A-Geng was a mason who fell from a roof before February. He didn't get hurt at the time, but later he suddenly started coughing up blood. He died less than ten days after coughing up blood. A-Geng's wife didn't cry; instead, she was happy, saying that she could never get ahead with this poor ghost. A week later, her four-year-old daughter suddenly disappeared. Her daughter disappeared, but she didn't cry or look for her; instead, she was even happier, saying that she was relieved. Half a month later, she found a partner and moved away joyfully.

Who says women are good at crying? These three are the women I have personally seen who do not cry. Although they were all faced with events that would make even men want to cry, I swear that none of them moved a stony heart. Humans are not made of wood or stone; how can they be without feelings? Yet there are women in the world who find themselves in pitiable circumstances and do not cry. Hey, truly amazing. But I always feel that it seems a little inhuman.

Fish and Wine 195

— Zheng Yimei

The other day, it was famous director Dan Junyu's fortieth birthday, and I went to congratulate him. Recently, Mr. Du has grown tired of the silver screen and celluloid life, and keeps several tanks of tropical fish in his home to amuse himself. The bottom of the tanks is lined with Yuhua Terrace patterned stones, and several stems of tropical grass are planted, their green color so clear. The fish swim among them, making one feel as if one is on the Hao River bridge. The most beautiful fish are the angelfish, with their flat bodies and long fins, patterned with stripes and delightful colors. It is said that these fish can eat flies, but I have not witnessed it. Mr. Du is skilled in oil painting, and his still lifes are remarkably lifelike. There are glass fish, their bodies completely transparent, through which their internal organs can be seen; and there are Lili fish, their tails a light purple color, whose call sounds like a frog. They are truly special specimens. Fighting fish are naturally belligerent, but since there is only one, it cannot engage in hostile action. Mr. Du drives it to the edge of the tank and shows it a mirror. The fish sees its reflection in the mirror, flaring its fins and opening its mouth, with the appearance of killing an enemy. Its body color changes, sometimes green, sometimes red, like a rainbow or brocade, like Shu brocade unfurling or a strange flower budding. No wonder the people of Siam consider fighting fish to be their sole entertainment. After watching for a while, Mr. Du treated me to fine wine. Drinking it, the taste was mellow and rich, with no dry throat or mouth. When I asked about it, he said: "This is Moutai wine, the famous brew of Qian (Guizhou)." The wine is produced in Moutai Village, Renhuai County. Due to transportation difficulties and exorbitant taxes, it is not easy to get it out of the province. In the spring of the sixteenth year, my cousin Maoxin brought back several urns from that place. Drinking it, the fragrance lingered on the teeth and cheeks for days. Since then, whenever I have good food, I think of the famous wine. I have not tasted it for ten years. One day, I happened to pass a shop on Sanma Road and saw a sign saying that it was selling Moutai wine on consignment, but I was too poor to buy it and take it home. By coincidence, the owner of a certain bookstore visited me the other day and asked me to paint two cover designs, for which I was paid twenty gold coins. I immediately bought five bottles from the market, each bottle costing four gold coins, which was exactly the right amount. After ten years of longing, my wish was fulfilled in one morning. What joy! I want to share this joy with you all tonight." Those present at the table were Jiang Zimei, Kang Zhuang Ziguo, his great-nephew Dan Erchun, and Madam Yin Mingzhu, all of whom were tipsy.

White Reeds, Red Smartweed, and a Flock of Wild Ducks 196

— Delin

White reeds and red smartweed adorn the scenery of early winter. By the shores of Taihu Lake and Dongting Lake, there are also flocks of thousands upon thousands of wild ducks. They seem to beat their wings like falling leaves, holding their heads high against the wind. Amidst the lakes and mountains, they weave a magnificent and vast scene. If you were to find yourself in such a setting at Taihu Lake or Dongting Lake and look out over the vast expanse, you would surely be stirred with aspirations of transcending mortality. But will they always be so carefree and leisurely? No, humans need to consider them as delicacies of the season. At this time, Taihu Lake is filled with many small boats, rowing back and forth, chasing after the flocks of wild ducks. Using skilled techniques, hunters aim their shotguns. With a single shot, the wild ducks fall from the sky, landing in clumps of reeds or on the surface of the lake. When you buy this "Taihu delicacy" from a game shop and happily savor it, you may often find bullet fragments in it. The skill of shooting ducks with a shotgun is a secret known only to the fishermen of the Dongting Lake water region. No matter how skilled you are with a gun, no matter how clever your shooting techniques, if you try it on the shores of Taihu Lake, you will be disappointed and unable to shoot a single duck. But the fishermen, as long as they aim, will hit their targets every time without missing a shot. Their methods are extremely skilled and agile.

In addition to guns, wild ducks can also be captured with "heavenly nets." Fishermen row their boats to where there are the most wild ducks and, using all their strength, pull up the large "heavenly net." This net covers the sky and comes crashing down on the lake. The wild ducks, trapped by the net, have no way to escape and are captured alive. If you walk past the front of a game shop, you can see not only bunches of dead wild ducks hanging there, but also live wild ducks crowded together in wire cages, a testament to the overwhelming demand.

At dusk, the neon lights of the game shop, spelling out "wild duck," tempt the vision and appetite of every passerby. In the chilly early winter weather, the rich savor the taste of wild duck and sleep on soft, downy wild duck quilts. The texture is so light and soft, and the price is very high. It's a wonderfully comfortable life, but the wild ducks that were still flying freely in the sky amidst the lakes and mountains today will be plucked of their feathers and eaten tomorrow. A heartbreaking sight for the wild ducks! The wealthy should not follow in their footsteps.

Literature and Art

Epitaph for Zheng Gong Yuanru of Yongchun 197

— Wu Zengqi

Gong's given name was Weinian, courtesy name Shide, literary name Yuanru, from the Zheng family. He was a descendant of Mr. Zheng Jie. The first ancestor, Duke Dunhou, moved from Shandong to Yongchun at the end of the Ming Dynasty and named Beixiang after Zheng Jie. From the seventh-generation ancestor upwards, all were diligent farmers. The eighth-generation ancestor, Duke Boliangshi, passed the imperial examination in the early Kangxi period. After that, those who passed the examinations appeared one after another, and the Zheng family became a prominent family in Yongchun. His father, Duke Weiting, had hidden virtues. Gong was thirteen years old and exceptionally intelligent. At that time, the Zheng family had ancestral businesses in Fujian. Gong asked his father if he could go and work together. His father agreed. Within a year, the business improved. His father heard this and was pleased, saying, "This son will surely glorify our family, I have no worries." Gong served his grandparents and parents diligently, and was able to win their hearts. He treated his elder brother, Duke Geru, with great respect. His brother was fond of learning but did not succeed, so he placed great hopes on his son. Gong understood his brother's intentions and ordered his nephew Shulin to study at Waseda University in Japan, loving him as his own son. After the Xinhai Revolution, the region experienced many disturbances. He initiated the organization of local militias to protect the villages, on which the entire township relied. Commander Yan Guangwei greatly valued him, and often came to Gong's home to consult him, calling him the "shield of Yongchun." Later, Gong went to Xiamen to support his son Yushu, who was raising funds. As he was leaving, the villagers blocked the road to keep him, fearing that if Gong left, the entire township would not have a day of peace. In the countryside, he initiated the establishment of a primary school at Jiaxi, which achieved remarkable results. He also founded Yuanru School, spending over ten thousand gold coins, all by Gong's own efforts. Gong was born in the fourth month of the Dingmao year of the Tongzhi reign (1867) and died in the fourth month of the Yichou year (1925) at the age of fifty-nine. He married twice, both from the Hong family of Nan'an. He had four sons: Yushu, Yulin, and Xianglin, born to his first wife; and Zhonglin, born to his second wife. He had two daughters, both born to his second wife, who both married into the Hong family. He had ten grandsons: Kuiyi and Qichao by Yushu; Qishen, Qixi, Qiliang, Qiqian, and Qitai by Yulin; and Qixun, Qiyao, and Qimo by Xianglin. Yushu served as the Xiamen Circuit Intendant, known for his political achievements and loved by the people. They will bury Gong on a certain day of a certain month at Changlunwei in his hometown. Beforehand, they came to request an inscription. According to Gong's life deeds, all should be inscribed. Therefore, this is a summary of his life, which is buried in the underworld, along with an inscription in verse: "In the land of Jiaxi, there was a virtuous man, whose benevolence extended to all things, whose righteousness established his life, who diligently cultivated his conduct and was always near the Way. Although his position was not prominent, his name will not be forgotten. Future generations will tell of him, as they look upon this steadfast stone."
