Swapping the Phoenix for the Luan Bird 199

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 9: Bad News Startles as a Beauty Falls into Filth; Her Fragrant Trail Leads Frequently, and a Heart is Like Catkins Stuck in Mud

Youmei, seeing the determined look on his face, deliberately calmed herself first, placed her teacup on the coffee table, sat down leisurely, and smiled slightly: "Has Cousin not known of Menglan's background since corresponding with her?" Guoqi said: "How can I ask about someone's background in a letter?" Youmei nodded and sat silently. Guoqi's face was a little flushed, and he himself did not understand why, his heart already leaping a little. He then said: "Just now, Ms. Li said that she had been chained since childhood. What does that mean?" Youmei said: "In truth, I shouldn't tell you. It's not as if it is some secret of hers that I shouldn't tell you. It's just that after telling you, you will add another layer of worry to your heart." Guoqi, upon hearing this, looked even more dejected. He nodded and said: "That doesn't matter. I knew long ago that she was a heartbroken person." Youmei said: "To tell Cousin the truth, in her eyes, perhaps only I can be considered half a confidante, someone with whom she can chat. In addition, she herself believes that in this life, she will not find a good companion. The reason for this is that her parents put a chain on her when she was young. Does Cousin understand now?" Guoqi said: "So, her parents have already betrothed her to someone in a womb marriage." "This is an extremely bad custom in Chinese society. I didn't expect it to fall on her head, unfortunately." He sighed after speaking. Youmei said: "Although it's not a womb marriage, the engagement day was when she was very young. She comes from a prominent family, and it's not easy to break old habits. She doesn't want to make her whole family unhappy for her own sake, and she also knows how a modern woman should behave. Amidst the conflict between new and old ideas, she is extremely distressed. We, as friends, can't help her make a decision." Saying this, Youmei adjusted her hair and looked towards the door curtain, meaning that she was afraid that Old Madam Zhang would hear. She then continued: "Having no other choice, she has to seek solace in books. Unexpectedly, Cousin's writing is very much to her liking, and she doesn't want to live in this corner of Nanjing City…" To put it superstitiously, perhaps this is the little god of creation deliberately playing tricks on people. I see it from the side and feel very sorry for her. I am willing to help her to a certain extent." She paused here, raised her head and thought for a moment, then smiled slightly at Guoqi: "I'm sorry, I'm very clumsy, and there are many things that I need to say, but I can't say them all. However, Cousin is a learned person, and you don't need me to say anything; you will understand that I am completely well-intentioned." (108)

Odds and Ends

Inner Mongolia, a Miniature of the National Defense Line 200

— Jiyun

Since the outbreak of the bandit rebellion in Suidong, the people of the country have paid extreme attention to national defense. In addition to doing our best to provide practical support to the soldiers defending the country, we should have a deep understanding of the current situation in Inner Mongolia.

Inner Mongolia was still in a nomadic state at the end of the Yuan Dynasty. The political organization was not established until the early Qing Dynasty. The Qing court unified the Mongolian princes and clans and changed the system to leagues and banners. The desert was often used as the boundary, with Outer Mongolia to the north of the desert and Inner Mongolia to the south. Inner Mongolia consisted of twenty-four tribes and forty-nine banners, forming six leagues. Among them, three leagues, such as Jerim, Josutu, and Juu Uda, consisting of fourteen tribes and twenty-six banners, were included in the so-called "Wangdao Paradise" after the September 18th Incident. The current rebellion is occurring in parts of the three leagues of Xilingol, Ih Juu, and Ulanqab, consisting of ten tribes and twenty-three banners. The so-called banner is equivalent to a county in other provinces and is the unit of administrative division. Multiple banners form a league. Each banner has a head called a Jasagh, and each league has a league leader and deputy league leader. The administrative power adopts a deliberative system. In recent years, the hereditary Jasaghs have gradually adopted an election system. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China (1928), the area was formally reorganized into the provinces of Rehe, Chahar, and Suiyuan. The localities were also the same as the interior, with county magistrates and police soldiers, etc., thus transforming their nomadic state.

The climate in Inner Mongolia is relatively cold, with winter temperatures below minus 40 degrees Celsius. Spring and autumn each last one month, and summer lasts two months, with the rest of the year being winter. Except for the south, the land is not suitable for cultivation, but animal husbandry is extremely prosperous, with pastures everywhere, not as desolate as we imagine. The population of Inner and Outer Mongolia is roughly five million, with Outer Mongolia having only one million, and the three provinces of Inner Mongolia having four million. Areas such as Guihua and Baotou are already as bustling as the interior. The Han and Mongol peoples are loving and indistinguishable from each other. The lower classes there practice monogamy, while the middle and upper classes practice polygamy. The first wife has great power, handling household affairs, and her hairstyle and clothing are special, which concubines and maids cannot imitate. Women are more diligent and thrifty than men, and their physical strength is comparable to that of men.

Mongols have been good warriors since ancient times, known for their archery and horsemanship. Children of seven or eight years old can ride bareback horses and gallop across the sand. Horse racing and wrestling at lama temple fairs are famous Mongolian competitions. The Mongols are extremely devout to Lamaism. Medicine, prayers, and mediation of affairs are all handled by lamas. If a family has two or three men, one must become a lama, so they account for more than one-third of the total population. The Japanese have been paying attention to Inner Mongolia since long ago. Manchuria and Mongolia have always been closely linked. There is a Manchu-Mongolian school in Tokyo that teaches Manchu and Mongolian to Japanese people for the purpose of deeply infiltrating Inner Mongolia. The instructions for Ren Dan (仁丹) medicine include translations in Manchu and Mongolian, which proves the Japanese research on Mongolian, which is truly astonishing. In our interior, there are many who study Western and Eastern languages, but those who know Manchu and Mongolian are truly rare.

Recently, the Japanese also opened the Hinggan Military Academy at Wangyemiao at the foot of the Hinggan Mountains. It specializes in recruiting young people from Inner Mongolia and providing them with purely Japanese military education, with the slogan of restoring the heroic achievements of Genghis Khan. After training, they are sent to the native troops of Inner Mongolia to engage in special agent work. This kind of inducement for people to kill each other in order to profit from it is their consistent policy. We, who usually shout to protect the integrity of our national territory, should now unite to support the Inner Mongolian defense line to drive out the despicable elements who are being exploited.

The Road to Health

— Edited by Kangjian Pharmaceutical Society

A Woven Fabric of Hard Threats and Soft Comforts: A Superb and Unmatched Treatment for Gonorrhea 201

— By Dr. Yang Daonan, Graduate of the Russian Labor Medical University

…In European and American countries, a domineering, perimembrane bactericidal method has been adopted for the treatment of gonorrhea… The latest and most reliable treatment is to eradicate gonococci with a gentle and effective policy of both suppression and comfort.

Due to China's scientific backwardness, medicine is always stagnant halfway and cannot move forward. Many novel medical inventions in Europe are sometimes completely unknown in China. Although this is due to the underdevelopment of medicine, the low general cultural level of the population is also a major cause.

Is the Future of Sino-Japanese Relations Really Not Pessimistic? 211

— Fang

The other day, Mr. Kawagoe Daizen from Japan came to Shanghai and gave a speech at the Japanese Shenjiang Club, saying (1) the Suiyuan incident has been declared by the Japanese authorities to be unrelated to Japan, (2) the future of Sino-Japanese relations is not pessimistic, and so on. However, although the Suiyuan incident has been declared by the Japanese authorities to be unrelated, a certain Japanese military strategist once had the tone of admitting it frankly. The so-called facts speak louder than words, we will not discuss this for the time being. As for saying that the future of Sino-Japanese relations is not pessimistic, we really cannot understand it even if we think about it a hundred times.

Japanese Ambassador Kawagoe went to Beijing to negotiate with our country's diplomatic authorities to adjust national relations. The period has exceeded two months, and there have been as many as eight formal negotiations between the two sides. The number of informal contacts between diplomatic personnel of the two countries is even innumerable. However, the result is nothing. The opportunity for negotiations between the two sides is largely at a standstill, so whether the subsequent negotiations between the two sides can continue to resume is still a question that is suspected and cannot be determined.

Judging from this situation, there are more pessimistic situations between the two countries, and few optimistic situations. I don't know from what point of view Ambassador Kawagoe sees the possibility of not being pessimistic? The right to be pessimistic or not pessimistic originally rests with the Japanese side, not with our country, because if the Japanese side abandons its mainland advancement policy, it can be optimistic. Assuming that the Japanese side is unwilling to abandon this policy, then it cannot be pessimistic even if it wants to. This time, the negotiations between the two sides have exceeded two months, and the reason why they have not achieved satisfactory results is (1) mostly because the Japanese side's desires are too extravagant, its arrogance is too great, it only thinks of itself, and does not think of others at all, (2) one side conducts formal diplomatic negotiations, and the other side uses military threats. This attitude is completely wrong. This kind of method cannot be applied now, and it has a bad impression on the national relations negotiations. Therefore, the reason for the suspension of this negotiation, the Suiyuan incident, is also one of them.

Secondly, there are two reasons for the Japanese side's misconception of clinging to this policy and refusing to change it: (1) The Japanese side is too superstitious that force is a panacea, thinking that with a huge army and navy, it can get whatever it wants and do whatever it wants, (1) Due to the wrong observation of our country, thinking that it is the China of the late Qing Dynasty and the warlord separatist era, it can be intimidated and lured to do whatever it wants. This kind of observation is actually insufficient understanding. For example, in the Suiyuan incident that occurred recently, the bandits and puppets were allowed to ravage the border city, and in Qingdao, the landing of the marines was made in the name of labor unrest. The Sino-Japanese negotiations have been affected by the Suiyuan incident, and the Qingdao incident has continued to occur. It can be seen that the Japanese side has not shown any signs of awakening from beginning to end. Can the future of Sino-Japanese relations really not be pessimistic?

"Literature is Useless" and "Literature Ruins the Country" 212

— A Dun

All literati like to emphasize the function of literature. Like Turgenev's Hunter's Notes, which promoted the emancipation of serfs in Russia, and Goethe's romantic works, which pioneered the Sturm und Drang movement. As for Rousseau's Social Contract Theory, it is the basis of democracy. As for China, it is even more extraordinary. "Literature is the warp and weft of the world" elevates the word "literature" to the ninth heaven.

In fact, this kind of statement is fine for literati to whisper to each other in peaceful times, but it is not good when the world is in trouble. Because at that time, the so-called usefulness of literature is just "ruining the country and disrupting the clan." Let's take an old example first.

"Jin Lord Liang was quite knowledgeable and admired the West Lake paintings of Liu Qiqing, and was pleasantly inspired by the osmanthus in the autumn and the lotus flowers ten miles away, so he changed his mind to throw his whip across the river. He secretly ordered craftsmen to write images of the mountains and rivers of Lin'an in the envoy, and the sentence 'Ma Wu Mountain is the first peak' (Xu Lei Yuan Tan)

According to this, the reason why the Jin Dynasty repeatedly invaded the Central Plains was all due to Liu Laoqing's "West Lake Paintings". Liu Lao became famous in Beining with his lyrics, "Where will I wake up tonight? Willow bank, dawn wind, and waning moon." It was recited for a time, and it was even called "Dawn Wind, Waning Moon, Liu Tuntian".

Liu was also known as Liu Sanbian, and his lyrics were all written for prostitutes and geishas, so they were extremely beautiful. Yuan Qi said, "Liu Qi, dawn wind, waning moon, can make seventeen young girls and eight women sing it with red ivory clappers." For such a person, with such works, he actually made the hero of the enemy country "happily think of throwing his whip across the river," which is really unbelievable. The Jin Dynasty was always a great trouble for the Zhao Song Dynasty. Yue Shaobao fought to the death, but still could not "return my rivers and mountains," and the reason for inviting the enemy was Liu Qiqing's few lyrics. Some people naturally think that the ministers at that time blamed a poor literati for the responsibility of "ruining the country." However, we just know that the ministers insist on saying this, what can we do?

As for modern examples, there are even more. A certain general said that the literature of brothers and sisters can ruin the country, so he ordered the prohibition of falling leaves; a certain writer even said that punctuation marks are also the cause of ruining the country.

Furthermore, although there are examples of literature ruining the country, there are not enough examples of literature saving the country. Mr. Lu Xun said in an essay "At the Crossroads of Literature and Politics," "The reason why Sun Chuanfang was driven away was because the revolutionaries bombarded him with cannons, and it was definitely not because the revolutionary literati wrote a few sentences of 'Sun Chuanfang, we want to drive you away!' This is all there is to say.

Mr. Zhou Zuoren is the most famous advocate of the theory that literature is useless. He said in The Origin of Chinese New Literature, "From the many words I have said above, everyone should be able to see that literature is a useless thing, because what we call literature is only to satisfy the expression of the author's thoughts and feelings, and there is no other purpose to speak of. There is no great motivating power in it, nor is there any teaching, it can only make people feel happy." In fact, I think it is better to say that all literature is useless. Because only by first explaining that literature is useless can it not bear the guilt of ruining the country. Otherwise, even the works that Mr. Zhou Zuoren said "are only to satisfy the expression of the author's thoughts and feelings, and there is no other purpose to speak of," like Liu Qi's "West Lake Paintings," will also arouse Jin Lord Liang's "will to throw his whip across the river." What else is there to say!

Therefore, I am shouting here, "Literature is useless!"

The Blind Man 213

— Yan Ting

After several days of rain, the weather suddenly turned cold.

I didn't go out. My wife came in from outside and said that the blind man living in the attic room was making a fuss again, groping around for Little Tiger. Hearing this, I opened the door and went out.

The attic room door was slightly open. From the top of the stairs, I could clearly see the messy pile inside: a broken bed, benches, a wooden table, a rice pot, a kerosene lamp, and a chamber pot. As I pushed the door open, the blind man had already climbed out of bed, hoarsely calling out, "Little Tiger, Little Tiger!" while stretching out his hands to grope around the room as if playing hide-and-seek.

He must have been thirty-two or three years old. He was unusually tall and spoke with a thick Shandong accent. He used to perform in traveling shows, but later, due to illness, he went blind in both eyes. He moved in here two months ago with his family of three. The woman was a young woman of twenty-six or seven. It was said that five years ago, she was skilled with a gun. After the tall man went blind, she went to work in a factory. She had gold teeth and liked to look at people from the corner of her eye. The other one was Little Tiger, around seven years old, covered in greasy clothes and black soot. For a cigarette butt or half a sesame cake, he would often throw punches in the alley to entertain people.

Every day, the blind man carried a foot-long rectangular wooden box, and Little Tiger carried a small stool in front, guiding him to the streets to sell Wenwang divination. The young woman, however, was not always home. Sometimes she wasn't home all day and didn't return until one or two in the morning, and sometimes she didn't come home at all. Although the blind man was concerned about her, he dared not disbelieve what she said.

Sometimes, around nine in the evening, when I returned from outside, I would see him still sitting on the stool, his feet neatly aligned as if selling divination, his back ramrod straight, tapping the ground with a bamboo stick to urge Little Tiger to cook. I couldn't help but stop in front of him and ask in a low voice:

"Your wife hasn't returned yet!"

"She's probably working the night shift again. I heard the yarn prices are rising, and the factory is busy..." he said, hurriedly reaching for his tobacco box and offering me the six-inch-long pipe: "Have a smoke, Mr. Hong..."

I politely declined and exchanged a few words before walking away.

Many people in the house had things to say about the young woman working a night shift on top of her twelve-hour day job. When the blind man wasn't home, some awkward women would come and go, and often men would be waiting in the alley. This was a fact that almost everyone in the alley knew, but the blind man was kept in the dark. He lived his life between his Wenwang divination, the stool, and the wooden clapper.

I stood silently by the door. The blind man blinked his blind eyes and then angrily gritted his teeth, muttering, "Little Tiger, I'm going to beat your mother!" He raised his fists and groped over, as if to land a punch on me. I knew he had made a mistake and quickly said:

"It's me, Mr. Chen..."

He seemed startled and quickly stopped, lowering his fists and apologetically saying:

"I thought it was Little Tiger, I'm sorry! It's you, Mr. Hong... Please, sit down. Little Tiger's mother worked the night shift last night and hasn't come back. The house is a mess, I hope you don't mind!..." He then slapped the bed loudly, indicating for me to sit down.

I sat down, and he sat down too. We were both silent for a while.

The stairs creaked, and Little Tiger pushed the door open and came in. His hands and face were red from the wind outside.

"Little Tiger, where did you go? Your father was looking for you..." I asked.

Little Tiger ignored me. He gasped for breath as he went towards his father.

"Dad, I saw Mom. She was in a hotel with a man. I wanted to go in, but the man chased me out. Mom didn't even look at me..."

The blind man widened his blind eyes in shock. After a moment, he sternly scolded:

"Nonsense! Your mother went to work the night shift..." Then, he remembered that it was already around nine in the morning, and even if she was working the night shift, she should have returned by now. He was silent, shook his head, and sighed softly.

Little Tiger felt wronged and wanted to argue, but he knew his father was angry, so he shut his mouth and looked at the cement floor.

Around midnight, we were awakened by the blind man's hoarse voice and the woman's sharp cries. However, no one got up, and no one wanted to pay attention to him.

The next day, in the open space on Huade Road, I ran into him again. He was sitting there with his back straight, silently holding the wooden box and shaking it; but I could no longer see his former excitement and triumphant air. Little Tiger was still in another corner, performing boxing for a dozen passersby for half a sesame cake.

Little Sea Ballad 214

— Lin Ji

The night at sea...

At first, the ship, as if drunk from the salty water, swayed as it moved. In the bumpy cabin, the stench of human bodies mixed with the smell of white paint. The Javanese woman sleeping in the corner emitted a piercing snore, truly a sound that disturbed my sorrow of parting.

This was my first time, embarking on this distant journey with the dreams of youth. I possessed a vibrant heart.

I loved the sea: "Go to see the sea when the waves are small!" I murmured as I lay down, feeling my whole body suspended in mid-air, swaying so violently! The fellow traveler next to me was also a young man, covering his slender body with a brown felt blanket, his tiny eyes half-open, as if dreaming.

"What are you thinking about right now?" I asked.

"Ah, I'm a little homesick!"

"How childish!"

"So are you," he propped himself up halfway with his hands, "I can see the tears in your eyes..."

People who lack travel experience have too much travel sorrow, especially since we were leaving home, going to a distant, unfamiliar place.

After everyone fell asleep late at night, I was still awake. I drifted through jumbled thoughts, tossing and turning until dawn...

The sea was most beautiful at dusk. It was the second day of the ship's voyage. I felt that home was so far away that I could only grasp it in my dreams, so I dragged my heavy feet to the deck alone.

The ship was now sailing smoothly, as if it had woken up from its drunken stupor. The waves were white, splashing more than a foot high at the bow, truly rolling towards the back. The wind blew, and I seemed to smell the scent of coconut groves: but surrounding me was only the sea!

The sun hung on the horizon, weakly sprinkling on the sea, reflecting golden light. There was a bright red glow on the horizon; facing it, I was reminded of the mixed-race girl who always walked slowly on Mango Road, always wearing red clothes, and in front of my door, she always liked to slow down her steps and sing—

"Mangoes are sour, love is sweet,

Yellow boy, what is your taste?"

But now that enchanting song was far away. I was drifting on the sea. When I searched for her in my memory, oh, I could only lean on the railing and gaze at the yellow, blurred sea...

The ship was not far from Singapore. I was eager to see that novel metropolis and rejoiced; but my slender travel companion, who was homesick, wrung out his wet towel on his head: he was sick.

I carefully looked after this young traveler and told him that a new world and new days were ahead of us. He listened quietly, there, to my low words—I had actually become a talkative person!

But, when my words stopped, he turned over and sighed:

"Home!"

"Why do you always sigh?"

"Hmm..."

Seasickness for a single young man was too bitter; his face appeared pale, and he looked haggard. In just two days, we had not even completed one-third of our journey, and we had already tasted the hardships of travelers.

I secretly prayed from the bottom of my heart: "May he recover..." and then lay down on the cabin plank, wanting to sleep quietly for a while.

When the sea is as calm as a large mirror, facing it, people will dream for no reason. First, I took a harmonica and played "Blue Heaven" on the deck, my heart seemed to be immersed in the sea, with the taste of salt.

The distant journey of a young man's sorrow!

The ship finally reached its destination. My travel companion had also recovered. We stepped ashore together, rushing towards our future...

Pick quickly. Don't stop. Be careful not to miss the good time. Get up early to pick tea before the sun rises. Pick until the moon rises on the horizon. All day hard work, bones ache. Pick tea until the fifth watch of the night. Choose carefully. Twist slowly. A bag of tea is then made. Red as blood. Green as moss. Everyone says the tea tastes good. The tea drinkers smile happily.

Movies

Hu Die's Recent Works 217

"Eternal Smile" Changes Style, Minhang Residence Under Construction

Hu Die's new work, "Eternal Smile," is nearing completion under strenuous work and will be released to the audience this month.

Regarding the content and achievements of "Eternal Smile," we naturally cannot make estimations before the play is released, but some of the actual working conditions are worth reporting. The first is the effort and meticulousness of the film's director, Mr. Wu Cun. He has changed Hu Die's previous style in this play, often using the most psychological or clearest method and explanation to make Hu Die naturally perform his expected acting skills. Therefore, after each shot is completed, the staff is extremely pleased, and everyone is sure that "Eternal Smile" is an extraordinary work, especially Hu Die's brand-new style in this film, which is expected to arouse the audience's surprise.

In addition, Hu Die's self-built residence in Minhang has recently begun construction. The drawings were designed for her by the scenery department of the Star Film Company. It is entirely in the form of a classical Chinese palace, very beautiful and spectacular. It is expected to be completed in the spring of next year. She said: This is built with a little accumulation of her hard work under the mercury lamp for more than ten years. It certainly cannot be compared with the star billionaires of Hollywood, but she already feels very satisfied.

Nan Jingying's "Luo Chou Qi Hen" 218

Sinclair Lewis's masterpiece Dodsworth has readers all over the world. No one who has read the book is not moved. Now Hollywood producer Goldwyn has put this masterpiece on the screen. The expressive Walter Huston, the protagonist in the film "Lincoln," plays the main role in the film. Ruth Chatterton, who was very popular a few years ago, has not been seen on the screen for a long time, and she plays Huston's wife in "Luo Chou Qi Hen." The plot is very profound, telling a story between the couple of a large entrepreneur. It is very thorough in its description of the demands of both sexes and the unspoken pain of love between husband and wife. The film will be released this Thursday after "Casting Love" is finished at the Nanjing Grand Theatre.

Shanghai Shenbao Local Supplement Automobile Special Issue

Eve of the New York Auto Show 220

— Nie Yu

All the new models of 1937 are on display, and the sky garden-style trailer will be exhibited at the venue for the first time. Ford, General Motors, and Chrysler will hold separate events.

New York Special Dispatch (November 8) The scale has increased significantly. The display area has expanded. The 37th National Automobile Exhibition, which holds great hope for the automobile business next year, will be held this Wednesday, European Armistice Peace Memorial Day, at 2 pm. The Central Palace of the Lansing Den Avenue between 46th and 47th Streets here. The session will last for eight days, closing at 11 pm on November 18.

New York Auto Show Emblem 221

The exhibition time for this year's annual meeting has been slightly changed compared to previous years. Sunday will be open as usual, from noon to 10:30 PM. The opening will be on the third day of the week, which is a new precedent. In the past, exhibitions typically opened on Saturdays and Sundays and closed on the same day of the following week. This year, the exhibition time, except for the opening day and Sundays, is from 10:30 AM to 11:00 PM daily.

Holding the auto show in November is the second decision this year, replacing January with November. This method was implemented last year. The purpose is to enhance the employment stability of employees in the automotive industry and attract customers to purchase cars in the fall. It is said that it was quite effective in both aspects last year. Therefore, the Automobile Manufacturers Association, which hosts the exhibition, decided to continue using November as the date for this year's exhibition. They brought new 1937 models with them, hoping that the market they desired would immediately appear before their eyes, something unseen since 1929.

The passenger cars participating in the exhibition will represent twenty American car brands and five American car brands, totaling more than two hundred cars and chassis. In addition, various car parts and accessories will also be on display. Seven brands of trucks will be exhibited. American-made cars participating in the exhibition include Buick, Cadillac, Chevrolet, Chrysler, Cord, DeSoto, Dodge, Duesenberg, Graham, Hudson, LaSalle, Nash, Lafayette, Willys, Studebaker, Terraplane, and Whippet. British brands include Essex, Austin, SS Jaguar, MG, and Lagonda.

Trailers participating in the exhibition will be participating in the auto show for the first time. It is said that there are many types. The entire fourth floor of the Central Palace has been designated for display. Approximately twenty-four or five well-known manufacturers will participate. All kinds of "homes on wheels" will be displayed separately, with no less than fifty models. This exhibit is expected to attract a special class of people, especially those who are fascinated by a nomadic or traveling lifestyle. The trailer lifestyle is currently booming. People in the automotive industry predict that its business scope will be no less than several million dollars.

One day during the conference will be designated as "International Day," which is quite meaningful and a feature of this year's exhibition. The participation of Central-made cars is a first. Germany, Sweden, and France have also decided to send official representatives to participate in the grand event. Individuals from countries such as Britain, the Netherlands, and Switzerland, who are related to the automotive industry, will also attend and have already departed from their respective countries.

On Thursday, November 12th, the Traffic Safety Committee of the Automobile Manufacturers Association will hold a banquet at the Commodore Hotel. At that time, leaders engaged in automotive safety will discuss future vehicle safety measures. The annual banquet of the Society of Automotive Engineers will also be held on the same evening.

Ford Lincoln Exhibition: The 1937 Ford and Lincoln cars will not participate in the national auto show. However, in addition to being displayed at the Ford General Sales Office at 1710 Broadway, they can be viewed at the Astor Hotel and the Jardin des Roses. The exhibition period at these two locations is the same as the national auto show, from Wednesday noon to the evening of the 18th. The Astor Hotel's ballroom and its adjacent Rose and Laurel rooms have been decorated under the guidance of Mr. Teague. The color scheme adopts autumnal orange, yellow, and bronze tones. Various body styles of the Ford V-8 and Lincoln Zephyr cars will be displayed in the ballroom. The giant Lincoln V-12 and Lincoln Zephyr models will be exhibited separately in the Rose and Laurel rooms. The Ford V-8 truck display area is the mezzanine level of the ballroom.

In addition to various new cars, the grand ballroom of the Astor Hotel also features other interesting models. One group represents the important features of the Ford V-8 all-steel body and "center-balanced" chassis. The so-called "economic exhibition" includes a huge animated model of a Ford two-barrel downdraft carburetor, a "red light" engine showing its cycle of operation, and the fuel economy of the engine in operation. Another display shows the safety features of Ford cars. A display on "comfort and beauty" will utilize a luxurious white sedan, cut in half for examination.

General Motors Exhibition: General Motors will also hold a new car exhibition at the Waldorf Astoria Hotel, with the same duration as the national auto show, a total of eight days. The venue will occupy the entire three floors of the hotel. The venue is decorated in mulberry and white, with a very novel layout. It is also trimmed with satin stainless steel. Various GM cars—Chevrolet, Pontiac, Oldsmobile, Buick, LaSalle, and Cadillac—will be the main features of the exhibition. Other aspects of General Motors' activities and related general automobiles will also be exhibited separately.

The center of the ballroom is a four-sided circular wall, made of translucent paint, with a 30-foot-high illuminated tower pillar. The base of the tower is decorated with huge custom-made glass mirrors. Through the mirrors, you can see the "traffic dynamics" of the cars. It is expected that the most attractive exhibit in the venue will be a "cut-in-half" car, which will be displayed in the most prominent place in the hall. This "split car" is automatically managed and is said to be the first attempt to show a direct cross-section of the operation of a modern car to the public. The work of cutting the car in half is a successful project of the General Motors Experimental Factory, and it will take several months to complete. Fisher Body will exhibit its new "Turret Top" all-steel body, which is standard equipment on all 1937 General Motors cars.

The research department of the General Motors exhibition will display a "living room on wheels." The purpose is to show the comfort of General Motors cars and the average family. The standard seats in the 1937 model cars can be converted into practical sofas. Other modern car living room parts such as stoves, radios, ashtrays, car lamps, etc., can be arranged into a perfect family.

The Carl Hoff Radio Orchestra will perform every afternoon during the conference to entertain the guests.

Chrysler Auto Show: The Chrysler International Auto Show opened yesterday. The venue is on the first and second floors of the Chrysler Building. It is expected that many people will visit in the next few days. The main products on display are Plymouth, Dodge, DeSoto, and Chrysler. The layout of the venue is quite distinctive, such as rotating exhibitions and invisible glass, which are unprecedented. The lighting is also very novel, and there are exhibitions of winter and summer air conditioning. A separate room is also opened in the venue to show films about the company's products. The exhibitions of Ford, General Motors, and Chrysler are all free. The admission fee for the national auto show is 55 cents before 6 PM and 75 cents after 6 PM, including ticket donations.

New Streamlined Long-Distance Buses 222

— Mo

Increased Riding Comfort and Power

The transportation business of trains, especially passenger transportation, has recently been encroached upon by long-distance buses in many places. As a result, several railway companies in the United States lowered passenger fares this summer to attract customers. At the same time, they have been making every effort to improve equipment, such as adopting streamlined vehicles, diesel engines, and adding air conditioning for heating and cooling. These are all methods to attract passenger traffic. On the other hand, bus companies are unwilling to show weakness. In the past, they only competed on fares and convenience, but now they are changing their strategy and making great efforts in equipment, speed, and comfort. We only need to look at the "Super Trend Buses" of the "Greyhound" line, one of the giants in the American long-distance bus industry, to understand that the progress of long-distance buses has been very significant.

These modern "Super Trend Buses" are manufactured by General Motors. They are quite different from old-fashioned long-distance buses in appearance. The front of the car is not sharp, and part of the engine has been removed, so the appearance is very unique. The streamlined shape of the whole body maintains a moderate style, not too large. At first glance, it gives people the impression of diffused power, solid structure, and light and smooth flow. The first batch of new cars totals 325 vehicles.

The exterior of the car body is decorated with metal, which is dazzling and exceptionally novel and pleasing. Because of the rear engine, the front of the car gradually slopes backward from the rubber bumper to the roof, which is very attractive. The driver's seat is located at the front of the car, which is very high, making it sufficient to clearly see the oncoming traffic and the road conditions ahead. It is indeed much better than the old-fashioned cars. This is due to his superior land pull and the green of the insurance glass's large windshield.

The passenger's position has also been greatly increased. Above the shaking money, noise and dust can be avoided a lot. Passengers can look over the roofs of oncoming buses from the unbreakable windows. In terms of comfort, because the "seat on wheels" is completely eliminated, all seats are uniformly comfortable. The vibration of the axles and wheels will not disturb passengers.

Although the passenger seats are raised, the center of gravity of the entire car is greatly lowered than before. In this way, extraordinary convenience is obtained in terms of safety and carrying capacity. The entire high-rise part of the car body has also been eliminated. The seats in the car are very thick and soft. The chair frame is made of magnesium and aluminum metal, which is very pleasing to the eye. The cushions are deep and soft, and the headrests are scientifically designed. There are also movable armrests. The seats can be freely changed in position. There are four different positions for guests to choose from. You can look at the scenery, read newspapers, rest, or doze off. Passengers who are tall and have long legs can also obtain considerable comfort in the car, because the legroom between the seats has increased a lot compared to the past.

Although the legroom for passengers in the car has been widened, the space of the entire car has also increased at the same time. This "Super Trend Bus" can carry 36 passengers, compared to only 23 in the past. This larger space is obtained by extending the carriage to the original motorcycle position. The carriage is spacious and unobstructed. There are no obstacles, because many hand-carried luggage are placed in the lower carriage, which is completely separated from the passenger seats, which makes it even more comfortable. Some racks are installed above the seats, specially prepared for guests to place small packages and other items. Guests can board the car from the ground with just one step. It is an embedded corridor that is the same as the length of the entire car. The seats are one step above this corridor. The interior of the car is completely modernized, with bright painted panels and metal trim. The lighting also safely adopts new styles. The car top is decorated with Mossa glass. The light is illuminated from the inside, soft and gorgeous, with a special flavor.

The engine power of the "Super Trend Bus" is very large. It is installed at the rear of the car, parallel to the rear axle. This installation method not only increases power and efficiency, but also has extraordinary quietness and stability in terms of sound and action. The vibration is reduced, and the breath when it is extinguished is also separated from the engine location and the passenger compartment, which is very strict, so the vibration is less. There are two compartments on the bottom floor of the car, which are built very tightly. Water and dust will not invade at all. This is specially used to place clothing boxes, suitcases, and large packages. The luggage racks on the car top, which were commonly seen in buses, have been completely eliminated. The luggage storage compartment has a door that opens directly to the outside, so you can put it in or take it out at will. When the car is running, the door is completely closed. The luggage transport capacity of this new car is much greater than that of the old-fashioned ones in the past. Most of the new car is made of sturdy aluminum metal, so the structural strength is very great and can increase the weight by two tons.

Overseas Automotive Talks 223

— Yu

American Movie Stars Buy Packard: Packard cars are elegant and luxurious, and have been favored by the propertied class. According to a recent survey by Mr. Asana, a Packard car dealer in California, more than one hundred famous movie stars in the United States have purchased Packard cars. According to Mr. Sang, Hollywood is a concentration of various beautiful and new things, and it takes the lead in opening up trends, which is related to the observation of all parties. The large Packard and 120 models are all there, which is enough to make outsiders yearn for them. Especially in the gathering places of famous movie stars, directors, etc., Packard is even more of a leading car at the time. Mr. Sang also said that Hollywood things, in addition to being beautiful, must also have the elements of practicality and need. Packard's style is exquisite and can complement the stars, and so on.

Car Radio: The radio business in the United States is developing rapidly. It is estimated that the sales of radios in the first half of this year have exceeded the peak of 1935. Production is up 15% to 25%, and sales are up 15% to 30%. Among them, the installation of radios in cars is even more improved. In the six months from January to June this year, the sales of car radios exceeded those of 1935 by 30% to 150%. At the end of 1935, only 17% of cars had registered radios, with a number of 3,900,000 passenger cars. It is estimated that the number will reach 5,000,000 by the end of this year.

Interesting Car Analysis: According to the "Automobile Facts and Figures" published by the American Automobile Association in 1936, the total wholesale value of cars and parts manufactured in the United States in 1935 was US$3,319,973. The number of cars manufactured in the United States last year was 4,119,811. The total number of employees directly or indirectly employed in automobile manufacturing and sales exceeded 6,600,000, of which 439,000 were directly employed in the manufacture of automobiles and their components. The wages they received in 1935 were $657,332,000. The number of cars produced in 1935 and the value obtained from sales were almost 200% higher than in 1932, one of the worst years for the automobile industry. The value of a car in 1935 was calculated by pound and horsepower, with the following results. The average price of a car in 1935 was 21 cents per pound, compared to 38 cents per pound in 1925. In terms of horsepower, the price of a car per horsepower last year was US$7, while in 1925 it was US$27.50.

Please affix your chop to the receipt and claim it from the accounting department between the 6th and 10th of each month, and the 16th and 20th of each month. The Car Supplement Editorial Department.
